Because civilians who see bad actor drones will likely dive their own drones into them. (I referred to this in <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/existence.html">EXISTENCE</a>.) We need to remember, when it comes to dual use technologies that our safety depends only partly on restrictions - or on a vigilant protector caste (PC).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Over the long run, what will make the crucial difference is a high<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ratio of good practitioners to bad tech users.</i>&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">Keeping that ratio high-and-rising is going to be as important as any investment in the Protector Caste. They complement each other.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== Peak oil… by outgrowing it? ==</span></b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Speaking of whales, here’s a quote <a href="http://www.greencarreports.com/news/1102255_multiple-trends-turning-slowly-against-oil-says-rmi?utm_source=SNSINEWS-new&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=SNS+iNews+Highlights+for+February+9+2016">from energy expert Amory Lovins</a> about how quickly an industry can change:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">"In the 1850s, whalers—America’s fifth-largest industry—were astounded to run out of customers before they ran out of whales," he writes.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Among the factors that Lovins weighs: “</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">the energy density of liquid hydrocarbons remains an order of magnitude better than that of the best batteries envisioned today, though electric cars use that energy far more efficiently.”</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== People Most Watched by the AI Elite ==</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://www.getlittlebird.com/blog/ai-is-coming-on-fast-here-are-the-10-people-the-ai-elite-follow-on-twitter" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="239" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-C0SJ0mmTvkA/VsZV6rqINgI/AAAAAAAAOd0/0pgG5fu2LfY/s320/ai-twitter.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Back to our lead-in story. These are the <a href="http://www.getlittlebird.com/blog/ai-is-coming-on-fast-here-are-the-10-people-the-ai-elite-follow-on-twitter">ten folks who the most selective&nbsp;experts in Artificial Intelligence pay attention to</a>&nbsp;-- that is, according to the network tracking service Little Bird.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">1. <a href="https://twitter.com/elonmusk"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Elon Musk</span></a>, founder of SpaceX and Tesla; co-founder of <a href="https://twitter.com/open_ai"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Open AI</span></a>, a new organization dedicated to making sure AI is beneficial to humanity. Elon is the person most followed by the AI thought leaders.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">2.&nbsp;<a href="https://twitter.com/MFordFuture"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Martin Ford</span></a>, author of <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Rise-Robots-Technology-Threat-Jobless/dp/0465097537/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">Rise of the Robots: Technology and the Threat of a Jobless Future</a>. &nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">3.&nbsp;<a href="https://twitter.com/GaryMarcus"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Gary Marcus</span></a>, CEO of Geometric Intelligence, Professor of Psychology &amp; Neural Science, at NYU.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">4. </span><span style="color: #0000e9; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><a href="https://twitter.com/bengoertzel">Ben Goertzel</a>, </span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">founder of OpenCog, is a prolific advocate for an open source&nbsp;artificial intelligence network.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">5. <span style="color: #0000e9;"><a href="https://twitter.com/DavidBrin">David Brin</a>&nbsp;</span>futurist, blogger, and author with a new book coming out in March called <i><a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html">Insistence of Vision</a></i>, which he says "will open doorways into possible (and mind-blowing) tomorrows and alternate realities.”<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">6. <a href="https://twitter.com/randal_olson"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Randy Olson</span></a>, data scientist researching AI, master curator of great content related to AI, data visualization and more. &nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">7. <a href="https://twitter.com/peterxing"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Peter Xing</span></a>, intrapreneur at&nbsp;Deloitte&nbsp;and co-founder of TranshumanismAU, an Australian organization that aims to enhance the human biological condition.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">8.&nbsp;<a href="https://twitter.com/singularityblog"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Nikola Danaylov</span></a> is a Singularity-minded public intellectual and host of the <a href="https://www.singularityweblog.com/category/podcasts/"><i>Singularity 1 on 1</i> podcast.&nbsp;</a><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">9. <a href="https://twitter.com/rodneyabrooks"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Rodney Brooks</span></a>, CTO of Rethink Robotics, a company that makes robots that collaborate with humans.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">10.&nbsp;<a href="https://twitter.com/rfurlan"><span style="color: #0000e9;">Rod Furlan</span></a>, a Singularity University alum who’s the founder of&nbsp;Lucidscape, a company "building a new kind of massively-distributed 3D simulation engine to power the vast network of interconnected virtual worlds.”<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">“Follow these people,” Sayeth the Little Bird site, “or ignore them, at your own peril.”<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== Paints Preserve Us! ==</span></b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">T<span style="color: #313131;">he&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.brainpreservation.org/small-mammal-announcement/"><span style="color: #298cff; text-decoration: none;">Brain Preservation Foundation</span></a><span style="color: #313131;"> (BPF) has <a href="http://futurism.com/cryopreservation-breakthrough-we-just-preserved-an-entire-brain-down-to-the-last-neuron/">awarded a prize to a team that used polymers to stabilize all the cell’s in a mouse brain</a> so it could be cryo frozen without (much) damage.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>This will supposedly preserve the location and strength of every neural synapse or the “connectome” which some believe will be enough to allow accurate modeling of all of a suspended person’s thoughts and memories.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Note that the goal is no longer to make the organic brain come alive again, itself. I still deem this approach problematic though.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">1) There is evidence that the synapse is not everything. There are signs of substantial intra-cellular computing.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">2) The need for freezing at cryo temperatures still leaves the stored brains very vulnerable across a century or more. The "preservation" thing will only become credible when you can put grandpa's fully plasticized head on the mantle - at room temperature. (See this depicted in my just-published collection of stories,&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html">Insistence of Vision</a>.)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== Inheritance just got weirder and more like the New Testament ==</span></b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cENV5CU-TsE/VsZhi4B5ebI/AAAAAAAAOeE/8ibP5j8sVwY/s1600/human-epigenome-project.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="239" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cENV5CU-TsE/VsZhi4B5ebI/AAAAAAAAOeE/8ibP5j8sVwY/s320/human-epigenome-project.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Epigenetics is revealing how experiences endured by a child can sometimes affect his/her sperm and /or ova in ways that then are inherited in a somewhat 'Lamarkian' fashion, by the kids of those kids or even grandkids. Changes in regulatory chemistry, rather than the basic DNA code, itself.&nbsp;</span><br /><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.somosbacteriasyvirus.com/destiny.pdf">In this study we see a small, isolated Norwegian region</a>&nbsp;that had cycles of starvation and excess that are very well documented.&nbsp;&nbsp;It appears to be the latter - years when good harvests led to records of "gluttonous" over eating - that apparently had the most severe effects on lifespans, two generations later!&nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Studying the massive regulatory stew of the human epigenome will dwarf the Human Genome Project:<i> "…the human genome contains something like 25,000 genes; it took $3 billion to map them all. The human epigenome contains an as yet unknowable number of patterns of epigenetic marks ... certainly in the millions. A full epigenome map will require major advances in computing power. When completed,&nbsp;the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.epigenome.org/?page=project">Human Epigenome Project&nbsp;</a>(already under way in Europe) will make the Human Genome Project look like homework that 15th century kids did with an abacus."</i><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Almost yearly, scientists announce one more<a href="http://futurism.com/scientists-genetically-engineer-mice-live-25-percent-longer/">&nbsp;intervention that “increases the lifespan of mice by 25%” or more.</a><a href="http://futurism.com/scientists-genetically-engineer-mice-live-25-percent-longer/">&nbsp;</a>&nbsp;Caloric restriction, various nutrients, blood exchanges with younger animals… and now by killing off “senescent cells” that have stopped all active division processes.&nbsp; Eliminate those cells and the mouse not only lives longer but appears younger… (much the way Larry Niven portrayed something similar, in&nbsp;<a href="http://www.amazon.com/Ringworld-Del-book-Larry-Niven/dp/0345333926/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">RINGWORLD</a>.)&nbsp; Scientists&nbsp;<span style="color: #313131;">discovered that senescent cells secrete a tumor-suppressing protein – hence they rewrote part of the mouse’s genetic code to produce the protein caspase when they begin secreting p16—this acts as a kill-switch, which prompts that cell to die.&nbsp;&nbsp;Clever.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">But also simple, and hence it qualifies as “low hanging fruit.” Any species that desperately needs to switch to a longer lifespan – as we did, half a million or so years ago – is likely to stumble onto this method and hence I’ll bet they’ll find we already do something like this.&nbsp;&nbsp;See&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/immortality.html">my essay</a>&nbsp;on why we’ll have to find some more difficult and un-natural things, to get real lifespan extension for us already long lived humans.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">== Science &amp; Tech news ==</span></b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Finally, a truly non-volatile memory storage system,&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.popularmechanics.com/technology/a19459/is-a-quartz-hard-drive-the-first-immortal-storage-medium/" style="font-family: Arial;">laser etching inside disks of pure quartz</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;- could have an indefinitely long lifespan.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Meanwhile. A Harvard team have devised a way to&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.kurzweilai.net/how-to-make-almost-any-shape-out-of-a-flat-sheet-of-paper?utm_source=KurzweilAI+Weekly+Newsletter&amp;utm_campaign=12ba9b2e7c-UA-946742-1&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_term=0_147a5a48c1-12ba9b2e7c-281972889" style="font-family: Arial;">make virtually any shape out of a flat sheet of paper</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">, using a fundamental origami or tessellation fold.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.popularmechanics.com/technology/infrastructure/news/a19454/google-will-test-run-internet-by-balloon-later-this-year/" style="font-family: Arial;">Google's Project Loon</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">has been doing R&amp;D on a fleet of interconnected, autonomous, cheap balloons that will soon fly high above commercial jets providing ultra cheap internet access all over the world. This is just one of several endeavors that promise an important open door to the world and cosmos for billions.&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">The&nbsp;</span><a href="http://blog.caranddriver.com/stop-everything-the-single-passenger-car-sized-autonomous-drone-of-the-future-is-here/" style="font-family: Arial;">EHang184 quadcopter</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">isn’t exactly your flying car. But it’s a step closer. One-person passenger hauling by an autonomous drone.&nbsp;</span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">A nice <a href="http://anewdomain.net/2016/02/08/daily-dozen-12-questions-vint-cerf-father-internet/?utm_source=SNSINEWS-new&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=SNS+iNews+Highlights+for+February+9+2016">interview with my friend Vint Cerf</a>.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Alex Steffen, late of Worldbuilding.org, has <a href="https://www.kickstarter.com/projects/1910818917/the-heroic-future">a new&nbsp;kickstarted&nbsp;project: Our Heroic Future</a> - that I have supported, launching the live-performance talk trend some way beyond the TED standard of a mere inspiring 18 minutes. He intends "a remarkable three-part live documentary. Each 90-minute show is centered around a talk, incorporating stage presentation, film and photography, visual design and motion graphics, sound, music and lighting to tell a powerful story of where we are, where we can go, and what it could be like when we get there."</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Give it a look. Sure it's similar to things I've been doing. But there's a huge need for future-can-do tent meetings!</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Revivals of our most important faith... belief in ourselves and our children</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Google wants to work with university researchers on </span><a href="http://www.eweek.com/networking/google-invites-university-researchers-to-collaborate-on-iot-projects.html?utm_source=SNSINEWS-new&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=SNS+iNews+Highlights+for+January+15+2016" style="font-family: Arial;">short-term projects involving the use of its software and technologies </a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">in emerging Internet of things applications.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">As every other part of optics shrank, the focusing lens – and the necessary space behind it – remained bulky and heavy, especially on space probes and our portable devices. Now comes</span><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.npr.org/sections/alltechconsidered/2016/02/15/466272218/bulky-cameras-meet-the-lens-less-flatcam" style="font-family: Arial;">a flat, lensless array of several million pinholes</a><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">, giving new impetus behind the oldest principle in optics, opening an amazing diversity of possibilities</span></span><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Humans and Neanderthals&nbsp;<a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/speaking-of-science/wp/2016/02/17/humans-and-neanderthals-may-have-interbred-50000-years-earlier-than-previously-thought/">may have interbred 50,000 years earlier</a>&nbsp;than previously thought.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">There may have been a small admixture exodus of African humans long before the main wave emerged. Here’s&nbsp;<a href="http://www.cbsnews.com/news/neanderthals-humans-mating-history/">a better article.</a></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>and about space...</b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #313131; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Located about 300 million light-years away in the Coma Cluster,&nbsp;<a href="https://www.spacetelescope.org/news/heic1602/">a record-breaking supermassive black hole</a>&nbsp;weighs in at twenty-one billion times the mass of the Sun, several thousand times larger than the mammoth that lurks at the core of our own galaxy.&nbsp;&nbsp;Long ago, it would have been a quasar. The accretion disc around the black hole would have emitted up to a thousand times the energy output of the Milky Way.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Mapping</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">asteroids is important to our future - or discovering threats to it. T</span><a href="https://b612foundation.org/sentinel/" style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">he B612 Foundation</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"> plays an important role in this effort. As it progresses, </span><a href="http://www.latimes.com/science/sciencenow/la-sci-sn-missing-asteroids-20160217-story.html" style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">the distribution of discovered objects</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"> appears to be pretty much as expected, except in one zone. Close to the Sun.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== The incredible forgiveness of our fellow creatures ==<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I’ve long been fascinated by the ability and willingness of higher animals to parse&nbsp;<i>among and between humans.</i>&nbsp;Of course we know dogs and cats and horses do this, on a personal level. But then there are the whales and dolphins and sea lions who will flee some ships on sight, but approach others either to play or (alas, often) to beg help with a problem, e.g. cutting them free of a tangled fishing net.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Elephants are special in almost every way. They know that some humans are waging terrible war upon them, poachers slaying them out of greed for ivory.&nbsp;&nbsp;Yet, they have been known to flee in the direction of game wardens. And last year, in apparent proof of advanced linguistic and memory abilities, a bull who had never been to an animal rescue center led a wounded comrade there, somehow (presumably) having learned of it second-hand.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Now see this video about&nbsp;<a href="http://biggeekdad.com/2016/01/the-elephants-that-came-to-dinner/">a matriarchal herd that annually migrates, utterly peacefully, through the lobbyof a tourist hotel,</a>&nbsp;to munch on fruits in the yard beyond. It is elevating – even uplifting – to realize that we are <i>not</i> hated, as a species.&nbsp;&nbsp;Animals seem to know that we are varied.&nbsp;&nbsp;And at our best, we are capable of being friends.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">(In&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/earth.html">EARTH</a>&nbsp;see the self-contained story of a brave young man’s confrontation with a merchant of animal death.&nbsp;&nbsp;And in&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html">INSISTENCE OF VISION</a>, several tales featuring “Elepents” – redesigned as the perfect workers in space.)</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;">== And finally ==</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Share&nbsp; <a href="http://www.tickld.com/x/20-jokes-that-only-intellectuals-will-understand">20 Jokes That Only Intellectuals Will Understand</a>.&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Some are pretty good!</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/03/voices-in-ai-and-life-extension.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)148tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-8288950451722110048Thu, 10 Mar 2016 20:40:00 +00002016-03-10T16:48:01.748-08:00george marshallhigh-velocity moneyjohn mauldinkeynesianslow-velocity moneynegative interest ratesNorth Koreatort lawA world of slow growth - the one "stimulation" that works<div style="line-height: normal;"><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 16px;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Gh8pmmMy1ZA/VtTc1gV6WTI/AAAAAAAAOjc/o8HIBiEF0OY/s1600/orrery.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Gh8pmmMy1ZA/VtTc1gV6WTI/AAAAAAAAOjc/o8HIBiEF0OY/s320/orrery.jpg" width="240" /></span></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Standing next to the planetary orrery at&nbsp;</span><a href="http://longnow.org/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">The Long Now Foundation</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;in San Francisco, the prototype for the 10,000 Year Clock currently under construction, deep inside a mountain in western Texas, designed (by Danny Hillis) to tick for ten thousand years. This is but one of &nbsp;</span><a href="http://longnow.org/projects/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">The Long Now's many endeavors</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;designed to foster long-term thinking about our collective future, such as The Rosetta Project (the largest collection of linguistic data on the web), Long Bets (for tallying future predictions), Revive &amp; Restore for endangered species, and the <a href="http://panlex.org/">PanLex</a> open source database attempting to accumulate "every word in every language" across the globe.&nbsp;</span><br /><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">What does this have to do with a posting about economics? We should be a people capable of trying different things! Looking ahead further. Perceiving what doesn't work.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">As Winston Churchill said of America - we humans can be counted on to do the right thing... after trying everything else.</span><br /><br /></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Stimulating economic growth ==</b></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">My friend, the (sane) conservative economist John Mauldin, frets that the Federal Reserve might soon follow many other nations <a href="http://www.mauldineconomics.com/frontlinethoughts/the-fed-prepares-to-dive">in offering Negative Interest Rate Policy</a> (NIRP) in hope of stimulating inflation and growth:</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fIhMHOP8tbg/VtSwtTM2s9I/AAAAAAAAOiw/v159K7vmhlA/s1600/negative-interest-rates.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fIhMHOP8tbg/VtSwtTM2s9I/AAAAAAAAOiw/v159K7vmhlA/s320/negative-interest-rates.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>"</i><span style="line-height: normal;"><i>Former Minneapolis Fed President Narayana Kocherlakota, who was for years the FOMC uber-dove, says going negative would be “daring but appropriate.”</i>&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="line-height: normal;"><i><br /></i></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i><span style="line-height: normal;">"He has a number of reasons for this stance. In&nbsp;<a href="http://email.mauldineconomics.com/wf/click?upn=95CV-2Fzl-2FpCQXO8jlWkmrRq5UVCJ29lFP4il8wgmrGmZDSANUIjzrwjyl5oqRh8r7G-2B5WBfe34JRdkNtW"><span style="color: #003366;">a note last week</span></a>, he said the federal government is missing a chance to borrow gobs of money at super-attractive interest rates.&nbsp;</span>Kocherlakota would like to see the Treasury issue as much paper as it takes to drive real rates back above zero. He would use the borrowed money to repair our rickety infrastructure and to stimulate the economy.&nbsp;</i></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i><br /></i></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>"It is an appealing idea – in theory. In reality, I have no faith that our political class would spend the cash wisely. More likely, Washington politicians would collude to distribute the money to their cronies, who would build useless highways and bridges to nowhere,"</i><a href="http://www.mauldineconomics.com/frontlinethoughts/the-fed-prepares-to-dive"> writes Mauldin.</a></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 13px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Alas, assuming the worst of the political caste is somewhat justified, but only because U.S. politics has been deliberately destroyed. Politics wasn't always completely untrustworthy. The "cronies" in earlier days built the Interstate Highway System and great Universities and steered our defense spending very skillfully and sent us to the moon.</span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 13px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Right now, the list of delayed and desperately-needed infrastructure repairs is so long that it would take ages to get to "bridges to nowhere."</span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 13px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">You know something like Kocherlakota's proposal is essential.&nbsp; Because right now the Fed has just two arrows in its quiver, <u>interest rates</u> and <u>QE</u>&nbsp;or Quantitative Easing. And both of them have a huge, inherent <i>flaw</i> in today's economy.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Both of these "stimulations" -- and the earlier magical remedy of huge tax cuts for the rich -- <b>all three</b> produce <b><a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2011/07/calling-bluff-on-debt-ceiling.html">low velocity money.</a></b>&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Money velocity is the elephant in the room. It is the reason why "Abe-nomics" has not worked in Japan, and why central banks around the world have dived desperately into NIRP... and why NIRP simply does not work. &nbsp;It is the reason why earlier Supply Side tax cuts for the rich failed to do anything but inflate asset bubbles, never benefiting Main Street. Equities get pumped up for a while, but the real economy gets next to nothing.</span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 13px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZTPZQY5PJIw/VuH0fs0lkcI/AAAAAAAAOmY/IJWooCyTJKA9x0rJyr-aSgLo7k9NQBuig/s1600/high-velocity-money.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="229" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZTPZQY5PJIw/VuH0fs0lkcI/AAAAAAAAOmY/IJWooCyTJKA9x0rJyr-aSgLo7k9NQBuig/s320/high-velocity-money.jpg" width="320" /></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Is there an approach that can apply fresh-made <i>HIGH velocity money</i> to the economy?&nbsp; Kocherlakota's notion offers a way to do that. By putting actual men and women to actual work, building and repairing actual things, with actual pay in their pockets that wage earners immediately spend, that is what makes money high velocity!</span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 13px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Indeed, there is every reason to believe that the endlessly promised Supply Side "magic" of increased tax revenues <i>would</i> come about, at last, by priming the other side... the demand side.</span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="line-height: normal;">To be fair, John Mauldin knows this: <i>“</i></span><i>Quite frankly, if the Federal Reserve decides that it wants to do more quantitative easing, I would much prefer that Congress authorize the Fed to purchase a few trillion dollars of 1% self-liquidating infrastructure bonds – or, as a last resort, to do an actual helicopter drop. The infrastructure bonds would create jobs and give our children something for their future, a much healthier outcome than the ephemeral boosting of stock and bond prices yielded by the last rounds of quantitative easing. In those instances, the benefits of QE went primarily to the well-off.”</i></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 18px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Does that sound way-too sane for the American right today? Do <i>not</i> make the same mistake &nbsp;foisted by Fox News, ascribing the current GOP frothing-insanity to some inherent flaw in "conservatism."&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Fellows like Mauldin show that there is a wing over there that remains occupied by sane adults... who are now blinking in too-long-delayed bewilderment at the hijacking of their&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">movement by monsters.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">The best move for pragmatic Americans is to promise such men and women a way out. A place at the negotiating table. A couple of cabinet positions. Assurance that the high-velocity path will be overseen by Keynsians who are as wary and careful and heedful of criticism... i.e. adult... as the Bushite mania was <i>not</i>, all these years.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">But they must give something in return. Their willingness to drop old, symbolic loyalties and incantations and help us fight down the latest confederacy fever. And admitting the obvious. That FDR and Keynes were flawed... but more right than not. They <i>saved</i> western entrepreneurial capitalism, laying seeds for a 70 year miracle. And if we fail to achieve a moderate-pragmatic reset, like the one they accomplished, then everything could go south, really fast.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Be wary of genuine enemies ==</b></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Listen to this... the Saudi oil minister in Houston frankly telling U.S. shale producers&nbsp;<a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2016-02-23/saudi-arabia-to-u-s-oilmen-cut-costs-or-get-out-of-business">his goal is to drive them out of business.<span style="line-height: normal;">&nbsp;</span></a></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh, I don’t mind a low price shakeout and some producers declaring bankruptcy.&nbsp; But their wells and other assets must not fall under foreign control, especially through shell companies.&nbsp; It is a matter of national self- interest for expensive wells to enter the US reserve, even if it means the federal government buying up some of them.&nbsp; That’s smart anyway!&nbsp; Buy low and sell high later.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Whatever. &nbsp;Just make it a matter of national defense policy not to let the Saudis buy-out distressed U.S. shale producers. &nbsp;Anyone who lets that happen is an outright traitor.&nbsp;</span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== No more torture ==</b></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 14px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Nineteen retired generals and admirals have signed a blistering condemnation of Republican presidential candidates&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.yahoo.com/politics/republicans-all-wet-on-waterboarding-former-164218614.html" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">who support the use of interrogation tactics</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;widely regarded as torture. The officers also scolded them for opposing President Obama’s proposal to close the prison for suspected terrorists at Guantánamo Bay. … and “The statement by the retired brass called Guantánamo “one of the most powerful symbols for terrorist recruitment” and said torture “abandons the principles that this country was founded on, compromises our position of leadership on the world stage, and puts our troops, frontline civilians, and all Americans at risk.”</span></span></div><div style="color: #0433ff; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 16px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Let’s be clear.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The senior U.S. military officer corps is the third best-educated clade in American life, after university professors and medical doctors.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">They are tested and tempered so hard, year after year, that (for the most part) they tend to be the most self-disciplined and logically focused individuals you will ever meet.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">And religiously devoted to subservience to civilian rule.&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">They are the sons and daughters of <a href="http://marshallfoundation.org/marshall/essays-interviews/quiet-adult-candidate-man-century/">George Marshall, who should have been named “Person of the 20</a></span><sup style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><a href="http://marshallfoundation.org/marshall/essays-interviews/quiet-adult-candidate-man-century/">th</a></sup><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://marshallfoundation.org/marshall/essays-interviews/quiet-adult-candidate-man-century/">&nbsp;Century”</a> … and while they tried their best to hide it while serving, upon retirement a very large fraction of them have let slip that they deem both Bushes to have been among the worst U.S. Presidents, ever.</span></span></div><div style="line-height: normal; min-height: 16px;"><br /></div><a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/extension/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.blogger.com%2Fblogger.g%3FblogID%3D8587336%23editor%2Ftarget%3Dpost%3BpostID%3D8288950451722110048%3BonPublishedMenu%3Dposts%3BonClosedMenu%3Dposts%3BpostNum%3D2%3Bsrc%3Dlink&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2F4.bp.blogspot.com%2F-Gh8pmmMy1ZA%2FVtTc1gV6WTI%2FAAAAAAAAOjc%2Fo8HIBiEF0OY%2Fs320%2Forrery.jpg&amp;xm=h&amp;xv=sa1.37.01&amp;xuid=0gf8CigKxCzi&amp;description=" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; left: 439px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; top: 18px; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/extension/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.blogger.com%2Fblogger.g%3FblogID%3D8587336%23editor%2Ftarget%3Dpost%3BpostID%3D8288950451722110048%3BonPublishedMenu%3Dposts%3BonClosedMenu%3Dposts%3BpostNum%3D2%3Bsrc%3Dlink&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2F4.bp.blogspot.com%2F-Gh8pmmMy1ZA%2FVtTc1gV6WTI%2FAAAAAAAAOjc%2Fo8HIBiEF0OY%2Fs320%2Forrery.jpg&amp;xm=h&amp;xv=sa1.37.01&amp;xuid=0gf8CigKxCzi&amp;description=" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; left: 439px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; top: 18px; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><a href="https://www.blogger.com/blogger.g?blogID=8587336" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><a href="https://www.blogger.com/blogger.g?blogID=8587336" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/03/a-world-of-slow-growth-one-stimulation.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)96tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-4521688581548944006Mon, 07 Mar 2016 22:27:00 +00002016-03-07T19:53:22.528-08:00NAFTAownershipreal estateshell companiestpptransparencytransparent ownershipState power must be supervised. And non-state ownership must be transparent<div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I've repeated: <i><a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2013/09/transparency-news-nsa-has-yawn-foiled.html">2013 was the best year for U.S. Civil Liberties in decades</a>... and almost no one in the media would report on it. </i>&nbsp;That was the year when the Obama Administration and several federal courts declared it to be "settled law" that citizens have a near-universal right to record their interactions with police in public spaces.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Some did comment on how this phenomenon was forecast in <i><a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/transparentsociety.html">The Transparent Society </a></i>(e.g. p.160). Including my predictions that (1) &nbsp;this would empower minority rights activists to finally be believed, and (2) the fight over details would go on for years.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Sure enough, <a href="http://www.citylab.com/crime/2016/02/there-is-no-first-amendment-right-to-film-cops/470670/?utm_source=atlfb">the battle renewed</a> when U.S. District Judge Mark Kearney <a href="http://www.thelegalintelligencer.com/id=1202750304941/No-First-Amendment-Right-to-Filming-Police-Court-Finds#ixzz411h1Zqmo">ruled</a> against two Philadelphia residents suing city police for using excessive force against them. According to Kearney’s February 19 ruling: <i>"</i></span><i>We find there is no First Amendment right under our governing law to observe and record police officers absent some other expressive conduct. …We have not found... citizens have a First Amendment right to record police conduct without any stated purpose of being critical of the government."</i><br /><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">In other words, if you openly declare that your intent is to use the footage to publicly <i>denounce</i>&nbsp;cops, then filming them is fine and protected under the First Amendment. &nbsp;But if you are merely observing and witnessing, or taping in order to have a record, in case you wind up being abused... then that camera can be seized and recording stopped. <i>"</i></span><i>This means that only photos and videos of police taken in the spirt of protest or meant<strong> </strong>to express some other message of disapproval are protected."</i><br /><br /><b style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">And yes, that is as stupid as it sounds. </b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;Especially since <i>the First Amendment is not the only basis for this essential citizen right</i>. &nbsp;</span><br /><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2011/09/transparency-amendment-under.html" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tX6A6sgpi_g/Vt4HcsdJBiI/AAAAAAAAOko/MpYSi2IaFTA/s1600/Transparency-Amendment.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">To my mind,<a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2011/09/transparency-amendment-under.html"> the <b>Sixth Amendment</b>&nbsp;</a>is vastly more pertinent! That is where the Constitution plainly gives any accused citizen a clear right to confront his or her accusers, to demand access to exculpatory evidence, and to compel witnesses on her own behalf.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The Sixth makes it clear: state interventions must not reduce a citizen's access to exculpatory evidence that might refute state allegations of wrongdoing. &nbsp;At-minimum any such state efforts bear a steep burden of proof.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Fundamental: Amid the huge imbalance in coercive power, between citizen and state, what other recourse has a citizen, than <b>the truth?</b>&nbsp; Denying citizens the right and power to collect validating information, to back up their own accounts, is not just a violation of rights in some arcane sense, it is a direct assault upon the fundamental logic and power of citizenry, itself.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">This is an issue about which we have no choice but to be utterly militant. &nbsp;I have a reputation for proposing many pragmatic compromises, and for having some sympathy for our professional protector caste. &nbsp;But this is the core issue of our time. Forget encryption wars and/or "right to be forgotten" and any of that other stuff.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">This is the citizenship test of our time.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"></span><b style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><br /></b><b style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">== Tell us what you own ==</b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Having assailed one kind of governmental power creep, let me turn and blare a warning about the potentially disastrous consolidation of secretive economic power in a few, private hands.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The U.S.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Treasury Department says it wants to know if some of the current crop of&nbsp;<a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/business/wp/2016/01/13/the-government-wants-to-know-who-is-buying-luxury-real-estate-in-new-york-and-miami/">luxury buyers are laundering money through their purchases</a>. They seek to pierce the confidentiality often sought by luxury buyers who rely on shell companies or limited liability companies to shield their identity.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">For example, the incoming flood of foreign real estate purchasers has many causes, e.g. rich folks in the developing world seeking to safeguard assets and to establish residency, as insurance in case citizens back home get fed-up, or in case even higher homeland muckities decide suddenly to change the rules. This flood has severely affected the ability of Americans to buy property. <i>Cash purchases</i>&nbsp;of real estate hit a peak of 33 percent in late 2013. Think about that. Many of them masked by shell agents and companies. And even larger fractions in New York and Miami (as well as Seattle, Vancouver, Toronto, London...)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2013/12/the-chief-threat-to-our-great.html" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-93WO1IbhgKQ/Vp8gHt74vwI/AAAAAAAAORc/kQ7fifCqrKU/s320/transparent-ownership-treaty.jpg" width="240" /></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Indeed,<a href="http://www.mauldineconomics.com/outsidethebox/chinese-sunset">&nbsp;according to economics guru John Mauldin</a>: “a Bank of America Merrill Lynch analyst noted that if the top 3% of wealth holders in China moved just 7% of their money out of the country, it would add up to $1.5 trillion.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I am so rooting for Treasury on this, hoping it will set a precedent for going after&nbsp;<i>all shell masking of ownership,</i>&nbsp;everywhere in the world.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">See my posting where I propose a&nbsp;<a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2013/12/the-chief-threat-to-our-great.html">Transparent Ownership Treaty</a>: If you own something, you must openly avow and say that you own it. &nbsp;That is only logical and reasonable. So many problems in the world can be attributed to murky title. Indeed, the Peruvian reforms of the great economist <a href="http://www.cato.org/friedman-prize/hernando-desoto/biography">Hernando de Soto Polar</a>&nbsp;won overwhelming plaudits from <i>both socialists and libertarians,</i> by giving poor farmers clear title to the land they had farmed for generations.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">No act could ever more spectacularly benefit stockholders and true market capitalism, than for shell corporations to be banned if they are more then two layers deep, forcing hidden puppeteers to come into the open.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b><br /></b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>= The Trans Pacific Partnership (TPP) and NAFTA =</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">And yes, transparency of ownership applies to issues before us, today. Such as "globalization" - a phenomenon hated-on by the far-left and far-right, but whose flaws never came close to the benefits - raising several billion people out of poverty.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Two international trade treaties are deemed top enemies by populists of both left and right – one of the few areas where rhetoric overlaps. But what I've seen makes me lean toward&nbsp;<i>support</i>&nbsp;for TPP!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;Especially since it sets several important precedents toward transparency of ownership.</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh, to be clear, I dislike many things about globalization as-implemented, even in the TPP, like giving corporations levels of "standing" in international courts on a par with nations. See where I offer an almost science fictional take on this trend, weaving it together with&nbsp;<a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2011/08/seasteading-some-problems-on-way-to.html">Seasteading</a>&nbsp;and other things you never imagined going together.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">But there are much bigger positive portions to the TPP. It welds the nations of SE and East Asia together with the U.S.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>It sets new rules on labor and ecology that <i>they must obey, </i>bringing them all much closer to responsible standards.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>It protects intellectual property better.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>Above all, TPP sets a new plateau that China knows will become the standard of lawful behavior, before independent judiciary under rule of law, and if they don't start living by these rules, they will not be invited to the party.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-P1iMitNgJfY/VsKvp_ZsVRI/AAAAAAAAOdM/cNu9Ad2u7DY/s1600/NAFTA.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="230" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-P1iMitNgJfY/VsKvp_ZsVRI/AAAAAAAAOdM/cNu9Ad2u7DY/s320/NAFTA.JPG" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Those who decry TPP point to NAFTA, claiming it responsible for losing some American jobs. And I will surprise you by avowing that's possible, even likely. Still they are shortsighted persons who miss a key point --</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">That it was and remains stunningly, staggeringly, spectacularly<i> i<b>n our interest&nbsp;for Mexico to become a prosperous, middle class country.</b></i><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"><b>&nbsp;</b></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">In fact, no single foreign policy objective is more in the long term interest of the U.S. No goal is more important to pursue.</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Moreover, NAFTA is the biggest thing doing that.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>It is happening!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>Rapidly, as we speak.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;(The plummet in Mexican immigration to the U.S. came not just because of recession, but because jobs are increasingly available at home.)&nbsp;</span>And when a middle class Mexico comes to fruition it will bring a myriad transitions. &nbsp;For one thing, it is intrinsically easier for a prosperous North America to defend a short border with - say Guatemala - than for the U.S. to build a giant wall against a poverty-stricken Mexico.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The latter ridiculous fantasm is the current limbaugh-dancer fixation... and let me reiterate - the whole <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2014/07/the-immigration-fury-one-of-many.html">illegal immigration red herring</a> is obsolete!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>Immigration from Mexico is now negative. Mexico is on the rise and we helped do that and they know it.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span><b>We are helping make another Canada and boy will that be a happier soft landing than any alternative.</b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Failure to recognize that aspect of NAFTA -- one that's simultaneously beneficent and pragmatically self-interested -- is a stupidity shared across the spectrum, from right to left.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>Already Mexico is importing vastly more from the U.S. than it did before NAFTA and that will rise as this investment pays off.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Come on, lads and lasses.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>You are sci fi folks.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>Try taking a big picture, for a change.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== But lest we forget ==</b></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b><br /></b></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Still, keep an eye on the prize.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">There is no other action that would better ensure an enlightenment-based, flat-open-fair-creative 21st Century than a firm international treaty on transparency of ownership. &nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">There are zero legitimate reasons to oppose it, unless you are a frothing Randian who actively wants a return to feudalism.</span><br /><br /></div><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/03/state-power-must-be-supervised-and-non.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)154tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-424260033868509270Sat, 05 Mar 2016 18:55:00 +00002016-03-06T18:26:55.062-08:00nasaSETIspaceWFirstSpace Ventures - and news from the universe!<div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">My recent space-related postings have been - well - <i>upbeat! &nbsp;</i>&nbsp;In that I believe <a href="http://nautil.us/issue/32/space/2015-was-the-best-year-ever-in-space">2015 was by far our best year exploring the cosmos</a>. &nbsp;By far. &nbsp;And <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/02/space-so-many-milestones-ahead.html">prospects for 2016</a> are superb.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Now, let's dive into some of those amazing prospects... and then remind ourselves and our neighbors that the sick, sick gloom merchants out there - (you cynics know who you are) - will <i>not</i>&nbsp;drag us down to pessimism and despair. &nbsp;We are a superb civilization... as human civilizations go... with incredible potential.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">All we have to do, to flourish, is snap out of this funk and realize what we are. We are amazing.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Cool endeavors! ==</b></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">First off, <b>congratulations <a href="http://www.spacex.com/">SpaceX</a></b> for successful launch of a major communications satellite to GEO. &nbsp;Big league credibility. And <a href="http://news.yahoo.com/spacex-launches-satellite-toward-distant-orbit-001415770.html"><i>almost</i> sticking the barge landing</a> was not same-old. &nbsp;Landing a first stage that had just flung a heavy cargo toward GEO is exceptionally challenging. Every one of these is historic.</span><br /><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">And helps us toward bolder things. Example: Space Based Solar Power SBSP is a way the United States can take leadership—in space, on energy, on climate change. &nbsp;I've known folks innovating and exploring these concepts for decades and vital arguments rage on. &nbsp;Indeed, we all have to root for land-based sustainables to continue their amazing improvements in cost and efficiency... and yet, we'd be fools not to invest also in farther-"out" approaches. Indeed, lately some of my friends have <a href="http://d3ssp.org/">made some real headway</a> in showing SBSP to be increasingly plausible as a future tool set for becoming an even more spectacular civilization.</span><br /><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Aiming to attract more companies to headquarter in their small country, Luxembourg has passed <a href="http://www.geekwire.com/2016/luxembourg-wants-to-become-the-nasa-of-asteroid-mining/?utm_source=SNSINEWS-new&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=SNS+iNews+Highlights+for+February+3+2016">a law protecting ownership rights of companies</a> based there that extract stuff from asteroids. The United States has already made similar moves. Last year, President Obama signed the <a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/114th-congress/house-bill/2262/text">U.S. Commercial Space Launch Competitiveness Act </a>into law. This recognizes the right of U.S. citizens to own asteroid resources they obtain. The Space Treaty still bans ownership of the asteroids themselves. &nbsp;But you can profit from what you extract.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">With the <b>Hubble Space Telescope aging,</b> many hopes ride upon the 2018 launch of the <a href="http://www.jwst.nasa.gov/">James Webb Telescope</a>, a vastly ambitious and potentially powerful endeavor that will flagship an array of marvelous observatories that <i>you</i> built, with half a percent of your taxes.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="http://www.astronomy.com/news/2016/02/nasa-introduces-new-wider-set-of-eyes-on-the-universe" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="237" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-pRk4Y85zK60/VtSK62iEmgI/AAAAAAAAOiQ/MMDxs1Q5xrM/s320/WFIRST.jpg" width="320" /></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Now read about <a href="http://www.astronomy.com/news/2016/02/nasa-introduces-new-wider-set-of-eyes-on-the-universe">WFirst</a>, a planned infrared telescope whose capabilities will be awesome! Only when you look at an artists-rendering of WFirst, do you get a bit of déjà vu?</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Unmentioned in this otherwise fine article is the <i>reason</i> why WFirst looks so much like Hubble!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>Because it is the first of two <b>“new Hubbles”</b> that were donated to NASA by one of the US intelligence agencies, when their reserve inventory of spy satellites became obsolete.
