background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; left: 26px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; top: 900px; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><br /><a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/extension/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.blogger.com%2Fblogger.g%3FblogID%3D8587336%23editor%2Ftarget%3Dpost%3BpostID%3D8050355085993726303%3BonPublishedMenu%3Dposts%3BonClosedMenu%3Dposts%3BpostNum%3D1%3Bsrc%3Dlink&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2F3.bp.blogspot.com%2F-MOiQ92t5W90%2FVtOWBeIyf_I%2FAAAAAAAAOiA%2FcAj7g9wi5sI%2Fs320%2FTrump-emboss.jpg&amp;xm=h&amp;xv=sa1.37.01&amp;xuid=0gf8CigKxCzi&amp;description=" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; left: 26px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; top: 990px; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/extension/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.blogger.com%2Fblogger.g%3FblogID%3D8587336%23editor%2Ftarget%3Dpost%3BpostID%3D8050355085993726303%3BonPublishedMenu%3Dposts%3BonClosedMenu%3Dposts%3BpostNum%3D1%3Bsrc%3Dlink&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2F3.bp.blogspot.com%2F-MOiQ92t5W90%2FVtOWBeIyf_I%2FAAAAAAAAOiA%2FcAj7g9wi5sI%2Fs320%2FTrump-emboss.jpg&amp;xm=h&amp;xv=sa1.37.01&amp;xuid=0gf8CigKxCzi&amp;description=" style="background-color: transparent; background-image: url(data:image/png; border: none; cursor: pointer; display: none; height: 20px; left: 26px; opacity: 0.85; position: absolute; top: 990px; width: 40px; z-index: 8675309;"></a><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/03/trumpopulists-what-will-be-priorities.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)142tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-1216796225136820724Sat, 27 Feb 2016 17:04:00 +00002016-02-27T15:15:09.466-08:00auroracolonizing the galaxyinsistence of visionkim stanley robinsontumbledowns of cleopatra abyssInsistence of Vision and colonizing the Milky Way?<div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Well deserved! SFWA has announced that&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.sfwa.org/2016/02/35732/" style="font-family: Arial;">C.J. Cherryh has been named its 32nd Grand Master</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;for her fantastic contributions to the literature of science fiction and fantasy. About time! Huzzah Carolyn. Truly a master and a grand one.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://davidbrin.com/tumbledowns.html" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Ckhf3cqlKh0/VsZtMG92eYI/AAAAAAAAOeU/gOSFySDWwzY/s320/TUMBLEDOWNS.JPG" width="238" /></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">I</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">'ve been asked to post online my recent story "<a href="http://davidbrin.com/tumbledowns.html">The Tumbledowns of Cleopatra Abyss</a>," which has been chosen for three "best-of 2015" anthologies... so here it is! Who asked? Well some of those planning to attend (and/or vote in) this year's <a href="http://midamericon2.org/">World Science Fiction Convention!&nbsp;</a></span></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><br /></span></span></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Also, it's a sampler-taste of the quality of storytelling you will find in my new collection, <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html">INSISTENCE OF VISION</a>.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">See this&nbsp;<a href="http://www.tangentonline.com/print--other-reviewsmenu-263/collections-reviewsmenu-337/3052-insistence-of-vision-by-david-brin">rave review for Insistence of Vision</a>. This one very, very perceptive. Only note the ticking clock. Just another couple of weeks for <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html">pre-order discounts!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></a><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Post-Iowa Notes: NYT Nobelist economist Paul Krugman </span><a href="http://krugman.blogs.nytimes.com/2016/02/02/post-iowa-notes/?smid=tw-nytimeskrugman&amp;smtyp=cur&amp;_r=1" style="font-family: Arial;">highlights ‘uplift’ in his analysis of the Iowa returns</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">. His point being that we should choose to be more ambitious -- the one core thought that Bernie Sanders has contributed. Can we ‘uplift’ our society, our civilization? The American public mood is addicted to downer memes, despite every statistical metric having actually improved! While science fiction is filled with many negative stories, it is the one medium where perhaps 10% of the time, we see real optimism and hope</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Next? Be still my heart.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Will some university lit departments get over their smug postmodernist claptrap and realize that the most American-spirited of all literary genres may deserve some attention, study and tenured faculty?</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Okay, okay, it shows that I truly am a sci fi dreamer.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Will we colonize the Milky Way? ==</b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">In&nbsp;a recent essay -- <a href="http://www.salon.com/2016/01/17/what_exactly_would_it_take_for_humans_to_ever_colonize_the_milky_way_partner/">There is no Planet B: We're not colonizing the Milky Way any time soon</a> -- my colleague, friend, and treasure of science fiction Kim Stanley Robinson encapsulates the reasons why he believes our classic fantasies of interstellar colonization are&nbsp;&nbsp;at-best naïve and likely forlorn, ideas explored in his recent &nbsp;novel, <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Aurora-Kim-Stanley-Robinson/dp/0356500470/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">Aurora</a>.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt;"><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Aurora-Kim-Stanley-Robinson/dp/0356500470/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Still, I do feel a need to explain why I quibble with my bro. Like me, Stan's writing is often propelled and driven by polemic, which isn't a bad thing, when you are that smart and shine light - as he does - on real dangers! &nbsp;Both he and I want to save the Earth and both strive hard for that. (I even <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/earth.html">named a novel after our world</a>; beat that for commitment.)&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-LDFV9VkZkUg/VefOIjmcY_I/AAAAAAAANQE/xwTtj3P6TK0/s1600/Aurora-robinson.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-LDFV9VkZkUg/VefOIjmcY_I/AAAAAAAANQE/xwTtj3P6TK0/s320/Aurora-robinson.jpg" width="207" /></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Alas, we differ <i>not</i> over general direction or sense of urgency - or a shared belief that humanity&nbsp;<i>can</i>&nbsp;improve -&nbsp;but over a matter of <i>personality</i>. KSR is (I believe) being progressively drawn into a leftist perspective of zero sum thinking... that it is a matter of either-or choices.&nbsp; Either we devote our whole attention to terrestrial sustainability or watch our support system dissolve under the corrosion of greedy human civilization.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Zero sum assumptions posit that attention aimed in non-core directions - e.g. <i>outward</i>&nbsp;- will diminish the value we devote to what we already have -- the only known place where life and humanity can flourish.<br /><br />Again, I share Stan's sense of urgency, and we agree about the forces that today are endangering all of us through short-sighted, proto-feudal greed. Our lists of worst-villains probably overlap 90%! Where we differ is that I see many, many positive sum paths before us. While I am not a fizzing optimist like Peter Diamandis, I avow that as many good things are happening, as bad, and that studying what is working is just as important as railing against what doesn't.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Moreover while the ancient foe of freedom and science -- feudal oligarchy -- is today's worst threat, by far, where we part company is that I see little to admire in the far-left's penchant for dismally simplistic prescription.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Circling this back to his recent article and novel... We see this failing in Robinson's dismissal of the very possibility of space - especially interstellar - colonization.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh, without any doubt, science fiction was due for a corrective chiding, that the galaxy will <i>not</i> be settled as easily as humans just moved-right-in to the Americas. In <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/heartofthecomet.html">Heart of the Comet</a> (1984) Gregory Benford and I explored how necessary it will be for humans to modify themselves, in order to meet any new ecosystem more than halfway.&nbsp; Still, Stan's polemical reasons for taking this position force him into an exaggerated declaration of near-impossibility for that hoary-classic sci fi dream.&nbsp; In his novel, <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Aurora-Kim-Stanley-Robinson/dp/0356500470/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">Aurora</a>, he shows relentlessly all the things that can go wrong with an "ark" style generation ship... then, at the very end, he off-hand introduces a technology (a highly plausible one) that would make generation ships completely unnecessary, allowing humanity to bypass every problem he spent 700 pages describing. See <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2015/09/nitpicking-recent-great-hard-sf-novels.html">my extensive review (and nitpicking) of his novel.</a></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh, just to remind you, I am nitpicking one of the greatest science fiction authors ever to breathe. And a paladin of our tomorrows.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I’ll be on stage with Stan at UCSD’s annual James Arnold Lecture on May 5.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b style="font-family: Arial;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== Sci Fi and culture ==</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://publish.lib.umd.edu/scifi/issue/current?platform=hootsuite" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-hKk4dWQ9PGg/VsaLa1jTliI/AAAAAAAAOeo/xXGq7186iTM/s320/cover_issue_23_en_US.jpg" width="247" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The first issue of the peer-reviewed, open-access&nbsp;<a href="http://ow.ly/XBTZ1">Journal of Science Fiction</a><span style="font-size: small;">&nbsp;</span>is up! Check it out! Also from the folks building toward the new <a href="http://www.museumofsciencefiction.org/">Museum of Science Fiction</a> —&nbsp;Science fiction is the story of humanity: who we were, who we are, and who we dream to be.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: 12pt;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Debates over “singularity” topics can be fervent and quasi religious, which should not be surprising, since the transcendentalists of conservatism and optimism are only channeling their millennia-old tussle with a new, scientio-techno gloss. Francis Fukayama and Ray Kurzweil fought it out, a decade ago. Now&nbsp;<a href="http://www.softmachines.org/wordpress/?p=1772">Richard Jones continues inveighing in Against Transhumanism</a></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;- with&nbsp;<a href="http://turingchurch.com/2016/01/18/review-of-against-transhumanism-by-richard-jones/">a review and answer provided by Guilio Prisco</a>.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">A&nbsp;<a href="http://www.slate.com/blogs/future_tense/2016/02/02/occupied_a_political_thriller_on_climate_change_now_on_netflix_reviewed.html">fascinating review of“ Occupied”</a>&nbsp;– a new Norwegian, near-future thriller about Norway attempting to shut down its own fossil fuel industry, followed by a Europe-approved Russian invasion.&nbsp;&nbsp;Weird, but I am intrigued.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Some of the most beloved movies ever were based on books. But just because we loved them doesn’t mean the original author did.&nbsp; See:&nbsp;<a href="http://mentalfloss.com/article/31001/11-authors-who-hated-movie-versions-their-books">eleven&nbsp;authors who hated the movie versions of their books.</a>&nbsp;I had more reason, yet am more forgiving than some of these folks.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">A fun and pleasant&nbsp;<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2vNBA8mHFf8&amp;feature=youtu.be">musical reinterpretation of… Spock</a>.&nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">And while we’re on music… I mentioned the score to Star Wars: The Force Awakens, elsewhere, but only with an amateur’s perspective.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">This brilliant&nbsp;<a href="http://www.slate.com/blogs/browbeat/2016/01/08/john_williams_new_music_for_the_force_awakens_is_packed_with_hidden_information.html">essay decrypts the score in fine detail</a>&nbsp;and suggests that John Williams knew a lot more than J.J. Abrams is letting on.</span></span></div><div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Szymon Sokół</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;offers up&nbsp;<a href="https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PL5C79B0CF2EF0B736">a beautiful compilation of Babylon 5 riffs.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;One forgets how beautiful that series was.&nbsp;&nbsp;Well written, breakthrough art and effects, fine acting, sometimes dark… but underneath it all, B5 joins Star Trek and Stargate and (somewhat) Serenity as among the very few optimistic science fiction dramatizations that actually believes in our potential.&nbsp;&nbsp;In us.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #181818; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Huh.&nbsp;<a href="http://motherboard.vice.com/read/a-jihadist-magazine-is-trying-its-hand-at-science-fiction">Science Fiction as vehicle for Jihadi Propaganda.</a>&nbsp;"The Unit" by Yuito Abdillah, published in the German magazine Kybernetiq. Any German speakers here feel like tracking it down for a review?&nbsp;&nbsp;“</span><span style="color: #1a1a1a; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Despite claiming that this story is a work of propaganda, what exactly the author is advocating for is cloudy at best. The group’s affiliations are not totally clear, but a representative&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.rferl.org/content/jihadists-launch-tech-magazine/27478234.html"><span style="color: #655daf; text-decoration: none;">told Radio Free Europe</span></a><span style="color: #1a1a1a; font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;that they “aren’t from ISIS.””</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="mso-bookmark: OLE_LINK3;"><span style="mso-bookmark: OLE_LINK4;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;"><br /></span></span></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/lifeeaters.html" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="247" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2NX9jSdfA54/VsaPO-NP40I/AAAAAAAAOfA/5RwL0PL8xoM/s320/lifeeaterspage2.JPG" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="mso-bookmark: OLE_LINK4;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;;">The <a href="http://blog.nasm.si.edu/conservation/uss-enterprise-conservation-begins/">original NCC-1701 is being lovingly restored</a> at the National Air &amp; Space Museum.
