, &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Suborbital vehicles such as Virgin Galactic's SpaceShipTwo, XCOR Aerospace's Lynx rocket plane and Blue Origin's New Shepard system will be put through their paces, as will orbital craft such as Sierra Nevada's Dream Chaser space plane, SpaceX's Dragon V2 capsule and Boeing's CST-100 Starliner capsule,” <a href="http://www.space.com/31568-biggest-space-missions-to-watch-in-2016.html">reports Space.com</a>. &nbsp; And so on.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">2016 might (just maybe) be almost as great a year as 2015 was!</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://korgw101.blogspot.tw/2016/02/cli-fi-bullets.html" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="175" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-BgUr-uycyCA/VrVlSbfnogI/AAAAAAAAOaA/MSChtVmjm0k/s200/space-exploration.jpg" width="200" /></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">This&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.spacedaily.com/reports/NASA_Reaches_New_Heights_999.html" style="font-family: Arial;">year -end review of NASA accomplishments</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">shows that even if we leave out the great accomplishments of European, Japanese, Chinese, Indian and other agencies -- and prodigiously impressive private ventures -- 2015 was by far our best ever at stepping forth into the cosmos.&nbsp;</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">See this awesome <a href="http://armchairastronautics.blogspot.com.es/p/history.html">visual timeline of space exploration</a>, charting missions into our solar system -- from Pioneer to Mariner, Cassini to Galileo, Juno to New Horizons (created by Olaf Frohn). Scroll down to explore the entire graphic.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://www.planetary.org/blogs/emily-lakdawalla/2015/12311322-planetary-exploration-timelines.html" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="148" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-jw7mgWubwsw/Vph-wDr4TDI/AAAAAAAAON8/ti86ib4geng/s320/20151231_planetary-exploration-timeline-version-8_Artboard-1_f840.png" width="320" /></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">How many planetary missions are currently out there exploring on our behalf... and where are they? So many that Emily Lakdawalla of The Planetary Society has made&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.planetary.org/blogs/emily-lakdawalla/2015/12311322-planetary-exploration-timelines.html" style="font-family: Arial;">a timeline chart to track them</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">. &nbsp;She writes, <i>"</i></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><i>We are entering 2016 with 15 spacecraft probably actively returning science data from planets, moons, and smaller bodies in the solar system. (I say "probably" because I don't know for sure what the Chinese lunar spacecraft are doing.)"</i></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Lakdawalla continues..."So what's the tally? <i>Akatsuki is at Venus, Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter and two Chang'e missions at the Moon, two rovers and five orbiters are active at Mars, Dawn is at Ceres, Rosetta is at 67P (soon hopefully to do a soft landing), Cassini is at Saturn, and although New Horizons is far past Pluto, it'll be sending back new Pluto science data for most of the year, so I'm counting that as still doing science. Another two missions (Hayabusa2 and Juno) are in their cruise phase; Juno arrives at Jupiter in August. Two (ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter and OSIRIS-Rex) or three (if you count the Schiaparelli lander separately) will launch this year, with their science starting after 2016. The Voyagers and other heliophysics missions don't show up on this chart."</i></span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">You are a member of a civilization that does this -- from pennies per citizen.&nbsp; We are sending out feelers.&nbsp; We are growing, at last. Wake up enough to be proud!</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;And let it motivate you to make others believe, this coming year.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br />Believe that we are a mighty folk.&nbsp; Who can.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #535353; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #535353; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Looking back at Earth ==</b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Most apropos for this time of year? I have oft marveled that the greatest gift of the Apollo Program came not from the landings but from the earlier Apollo 8 mission, the first in which humans broke the bonds of Earth.&nbsp; It happened in December of 1968 - twelve crazed and frenetic months that brought most Americans -- and most of the world -- to the brink of exhaustion and despair. Yes, great music washed over us in a veritable tsunami... as did tragedies, war, invasions, assassinations, riots, betrayals, and fed-up demands for transformation.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Only then, at the very end of that awful year, a final token arrived -- like a gleam of hope shining at the bottom of Pandora’s Box...when the Apollo 8 astronauts brought home that first perfect image of the Earth, floating as a blue marble in the vast desert of space. A picture that moved all but the most cynical hearts and changed forever our outlook towards this fragile oasis world.</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-J8RHUA-tUts/Vph9btCpVQI/AAAAAAAAONw/uSFjLW6a3ck/s1600/920x920.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-J8RHUA-tUts/Vph9btCpVQI/AAAAAAAAONw/uSFjLW6a3ck/s320/920x920.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">Now that image has been surpassed in beauty (an we can hope – effectiveness.) Even more gorgeous in contrast — and almost the final space news of a spectacular year — is <a href="http://www.chron.com/about/article/NASA-releases-stunning-new-image-of-Earth-taken-6713006.php.">the <span style="color: #1a1a1a;">composite image that </span>NASA </a><span style="color: #1a1a1a;"><a href="http://www.chron.com/about/article/NASA-releases-stunning-new-image-of-Earth-taken-6713006.php.">released</a> </span>on December 19<span style="color: #1a1a1a;">, taken by the Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter, as it passed about 83 miles above a lunar crater. Same theme, but a timely reminder.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== More space updates ==</b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">See this: the recent&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.theverge.com/2016/1/12/10755860/spacex-reusable-rocket-landing-falcon-9-video-incubus" style="font-family: Arial;">SpaceX feat put to music by Incubus.</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Curiosity is the first spacecraft to study active sand dunes on another planet. </span><a href="http://spaceflightnow.com/2015/12/13/curiosity-rover-reaches-martian-sand-dunes/" style="font-family: Arial;">Amazing images</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"> of the next milestone as our robot envoy climbs the slopes of immense Mount Sharp.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Be careful in there.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">A</span><a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/panorama-mars-dune-curiosity_568c95c3e4b0a2b6fb6ddbbc" style="font-family: Arial;">&nbsp;panorama taken by Curiosity Rover from atop a Martian dune</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">, is enthralling in many ways, not least of which is the Dali-like surrealistic warping of the probe itself.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #2a2a2a;">&nbsp;Cassini snapped Saturn’s moon Enceladus drift in front of the larger moon Tethys in near-perfect alignment.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span><a href="http://news.discovery.com/space/astronomy/saturn-moons-align-almost-to-perfection-photo-151214.htm">See the gorgeous photos.</a> Plus a great shot of the Hexagon at Saturn’s pole, and of Titan’s black, organic sand dunes.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Now known to contain </span><a href="http://news.discovery.com/space/saturn-geyser-moon-hiding-global-ocean-150916.htm"><b><span style="color: #114769; text-decoration: none;">a sub-surface ocean beneath an icy crust,</span></b></a><span style="color: #2a2a2a;"> the small moon is thought to possess the ingredients for life. Cassini had its last ever flyby of Enceladus on Dec 19.</span><o:p></o:p></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #2a2a2a;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #2a2a2a;">NASA's New Horizons mission sends back <a href="http://news.discovery.com/space/the-amazing-floating-hill-sized-icebergs-of-pluto-160204.htm">images of icebergs on Pluto</a> -- floating atop a sea of frozen nitrogen!</span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><span style="color: #2a2a2a; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Important News.&nbsp;&nbsp;The US Department of Energy is cautiously and carefully, for the first time in 30 years, again making Plutonium 238, the chief ingredient not of bombs, but of&nbsp;<a href="http://www.csmonitor.com/Science/2015/1223/Department-of-Energy-begins-making-plutonium-destined-for-deep-space">the best power systems for long range NASA interplanetary probes.</a></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Human-Spaceflight-Stars-Louis-Friedman/dp/0816531463/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-946YhIQy8-0/VqgmSjSKGtI/AAAAAAAAOVw/5d0RS608sR4/s320/human-spaceflight.jpg" width="213" /></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">An ambitious future for human exploration of the solar system and beyond is explored in a new book by Louis Friedman, co-founder of The Planetary Society: </span><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Human-Spaceflight-Stars-Louis-Friedman/dp/0816531463/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20" style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">Human Spaceflight: From Mars to the Stars</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">.&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><span style="color: #2a2a2a; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">This should have made my list of spectacular space accomplishments in 2015.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Phil Plait waxes poetical and gushes about the way</span><a href="http://www.slate.com/blogs/bad_astronomy/2016/01/14/gravity_map_of_the_ocean_floor_reveals_new_features.html" style="font-family: Arial;">&nbsp;scientists have used tiny variations in ocean surface gravity to map in great detail&nbsp;</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">the topography of mountains, chasms and spreading ridges along the ocean bottoms.</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>And finally...</b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">While NASA's new <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/innovations/wp/2016/01/13/how-nasas-planetary-defense-officer-will-protect-earth-from-asteroids/">Planetary Defense Office will protect earth from asteroids</a>....see this <a href="https://www.facebook.com/notes/b612/our-response-to-the-nasa-planetary-defense-office/557243204430971?utm_content=buffer97259&amp;utm_medium=social&amp;utm_source=twitter.com&amp;utm_campaign=buffer">response from the B6-12 Foundation.</a></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">... the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/dr-yousaf-butt-/hypersonic-nuclear-arms-race_b_8700510.html?utm_hp_ref=world">Hypersonic Nuclear Arms Race</a>&nbsp;is on, as world powers develop boost-and-glide entry vehicles that can dodge and evade and accurately target sites across the globe.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">The Cold War Era statesmen and Gorbachev gave us a breather but the doom foreseen at Trinity Site in 1945 still lurks.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">We have to grow up.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">Oh, and while we're at it. The best way to build a Death Star... is to&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.wired.com/2015/12/nasa-death-star-asteroid/" style="font-family: Arial;">construct one out of an already-existing asteroid</a></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;">.</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot;;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Let's keep it all in the open, boys 'n girls. &nbsp;Play nice. &nbsp;There's candy - and much-needed vitamin-science - for everyone.</span></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== PS... ==</b></span></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I'll chime in - at the end - with my comments on the New Hampshire Primary. But first ... Seattle Venture Capitalist <a href="http://www.dennyhillcapital.com/team/russell-daggett">Russ Daggatt </a>is<i> big on competitive enterprise</i>.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">So why is he – along with nearly all of the tech mavens and moguls – a democrat?</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>Results.</b> Outcomes that can be measured and compared, and under which Republican governance has proved an utter disaster for market economies and the United States, while most metrics <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">improved</i>markedly across both the Obama and Clinton Administrations.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">This plus the blatant truth that – were he alive today – the oligarchy-hating founder of modern market economics, <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2013/11/liberals-you-must-reclaim-adam-smith.html">Adam Smith, would be a democrat</a>, too.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I go into comparison of outcomes in my own way <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2014/06/so-do-outcomes-matter-more-than-rhetoric.html">elsewhere</a>.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">But let’s give the floor to Russ, whose long list of statistical comparisons bears <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">no overlap</i> at all with my own!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>And yet his scan reaches the same</span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;conclusion</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">. If you want market economies to fail and if you are truly suicidal, for the sake of wrathful dogma, then you should vote republican.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Now, over to Russ Daggatt’s missive:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== The Daggatt Dare ==<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">What's incredible is this apparently widespread sense of dissatisfaction. I attribute it to the relentless right wing media Wurlitzer, on one side, and cowardly or cynical Democrats, on the other side. &nbsp;Whatever the cause, it really is long overdue for some of to speak up and tout the <i>extraordinary success of the Obama presidency</i>. (The Reagan presidency was far less successful and was scandal ridden. But Republicans and their alternative media spent decades spinning it into a legendary success.)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-G5dttQOsCrk/Vra8OFvHVDI/AAAAAAAAOak/b0HMB4EnmtU/s1600/metric-obama.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><img border="0" height="205" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-G5dttQOsCrk/Vra8OFvHVDI/AAAAAAAAOak/b0HMB4EnmtU/s320/metric-obama.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Let me take the obverse of David Brin’s <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2015/06/the-name-one-exception-challenge.html">challenge to Republicans</a> to cite any meaningful metric that improved under Bush.&nbsp; <i>Name any meaningful metric that got worse under President Obama</i>:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">When President Obama took office, the economy was declining at a 9% rate and shedding 800,000 jobs a month and we had a $1.4 trillion deficit. Since then, the U.S. has experienced the strongest recovery from the Great Recession of any major industrialized country. In fact, we are the locomotive pulling the rest of the world ahead.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The Recovery Act, in addition to boosting aggregate demand, spurred 45 states to undertake reforms to their education systems. It prompted doctors and hospitals to shift to electronic medical records and provided $90 billion in funding for green energy sources. The portion of the stimulus that lent capital to unproven clean energy firms (which came under withering assault from Republicans, who relentlessly touted the failure of Solyndra, just one firm out of scores that received loans) is projected to <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">earn taxpayers a net $5 billion.</i> Thanks to public investment in the U.S. and abroad, solar energy has undergone revolutionary growth, with <i>capacity growing 130-fold</i> since Obama took office.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="yiv0795941630msonormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Oh, and here is some great <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2016-02-04/renewables-top-fossil-fuels-as-biggest-source-of-new-u-s-power">data on the revolution in renewable energy</a> under President Obama.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">President Obama <i>saved the U.S. auto industry</i> (and with it, millions of jobs) which just set new sales records in 2015. At the same time, new (CAFÉ) regulations that were blocked for 25 years by the GOP are making autos cleaner and more energy efficient, saving drivers billions.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">After losing 463,000 private sector jobs during eight years under Bush, we have had a record 70 consecutive months of private sector job growth (beating the old record of 51 months), adding over 14 million new jobs. (And during that time, part-time jobs and minimum wage jobs have actually declined. Which means that more than 100% of the new jobs have been full-time jobs paying more than the minimum wage – despite the minimum wage going up under President Obama.) Unemployment has fallen in half, from 10.0% to 5.0%.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Inflation over the last 12 months has been 0.6%. (The core rate, excluding food and energy, has gone up 1.4%.) Under President Obama, we’ve had the lowest inflation in 50 years. The dollar is up 15% under President Obama (after declining 20% under Bush).<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The federal deficit was <i>$1.4 trillion</i> when President Obama took office. It was <i>$439 billion</i> last year – a decline of more than two-thirds. -- But the more relevant metric is the deficit as a <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">percentage of GDP</i>, which peaked at 9.8% as President Obama took office. Last year it was 2.4% - a decline of more than three-quarters and lower than its average over the last 50 years. <i>It is now lower than the nominal growth of GDP,</i> which means total federal debt is <i>declining</i> as a share of the economy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>In other words, much the same as happened under Bill Clinton.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>So who are the responsible ones?<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;verdana&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: x-small;">(<b>Brin aside: </b>see my own simple chart revealing the <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2014/06/so-do-outcomes-matter-more-than-rhetoric.html"><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Second Derivative of Deficit Spending</i> </a>and how blatant it is that democrats are vastly vastly and vastly more fiscally prudent than republicans. Refute my chart if you can! )</span><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The number of Americans without health insurance has declined by 17 million or more, and since the passage of the Affordable Care Act<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"> health care costs have increased at their slowest rate </i>since records have been kept.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Oh, and by the way, what is your gripe again, Republicans? Obamacare started out as your own… damn… plan.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-e3Ai3zIpAFM/Vra7ufV46VI/AAAAAAAAOag/d8QMaRYklfA/s1600/S%2526P500-obama.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><img border="0" height="239" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-e3Ai3zIpAFM/Vra7ufV46VI/AAAAAAAAOag/d8QMaRYklfA/s320/S%2526P500-obama.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The S&amp;P 500 has more than doubled under President Obama. (It went down 37% over eight years under Bush.) Corporate profits are at record levels.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Dodd-Frank required that banks hold more capital, derivatives must be traded openly on exchanges, large institutions must separate their riskiest forms of trading, and any too-big-to-fail institution must create an advance plan for systemic failure. The law also created the Consumer Financial Protection Bureau, which protects customers from financial industry abuses in much the same way as the Food and Drug Administration ensures the safety of our food.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><br /></i></b></span><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Granted</i></b> that Dodd-Frank didn’t go far enough in reducing the too-big-to-fail risk and other financial sector sins. So, replace this Congress to fix that.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Undocumented immigrants in the country have <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">declined</i> from 12 million to 11 million. Net migration from Mexico has actually turned <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">negative</i>. At the same time, in the face of Congressional inaction on comprehensive immigration reform, President Obama established enforcement priorities that would allow “Dreamers” who came to this country as young children, and who have no serious criminal record, to stay and work in the country, while focusing limited enforcement resources on criminals and recent arrivals.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Again, and your complaint is…?<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: x-small;"><b>(Brin aside:</b> The immigration matter is even more skewed than this. Always (except right after 9/11), republican presidents <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">cut</i> the Border Patrol and dem presidents bolster it, diametrically opposite to their constituent dogmas.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Why?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Find out <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2014/07/the-immigration-fury-one-of-many.html">here</a>.)&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Under President Obama, U.S. oil and gas production has doubled, and we have become the world's largest producer of petroleum products. That has driven down the price of oil, benefiting US consumers while crippling the economies of countries like Russia and Iran.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The cost of electricity generation using wind power fell 61 percent from 2009 to 2015, while the cost of solar power fell 82 percent. These numbers show progress at rates we normally only expect to see for information technology. And they put the cost of renewable energy into a range where it’s competitive with fossil fuels, even at low oil prices.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">On the most important long-term issue facing the planet, climate change, President Obama reached a major climate agreement with China, which resulted in the first-ever international agreement by industrialized and developing countries alike to curtail their emissions (an agreement made easier by the revolutionary improvements in green energy, which could allow developing economies to leapfrog straight past the dirty energy stage). The success of this agreement will take decades to measure, but it could well go down in history as Obama’s most significant legacy. He helped jumpstart this historic agreement by enacting new Clean Power Rules that will reduce greenhouse gases and other pollutants.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Under Obama, the U.S. resumed launching climate study satellites that were canceled or sabotaged by the previous administration. You are free to proclaim that his support of scientists is wrong and the House “Science” Committee’s seething hatred of science is appropriate.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>But you’d be very wrong.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">President Obama took office with almost 200,000 troops on the ground in Iraq and Afghanistan, as the U.S. was bogged down in the two longest wars in its history. Multiple tours of duty of not only active duty soldiers, but also reserves and national guard troops, left our state of military readiness the worst it’s been in our lifetime. Today we have about 10,000 troops in those countries and our military readiness is nearly restored to the 100% level at the end of the Clinton administration. (Does anyone really wish we had still had hundreds of thousands of U.S. soldiers mired down in the midst of a regional Shia-Sunni intra-religious war?)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">In 2008, before President Obama took office, Cheney insisted that we had to attack Iran with Iran only a few months away from a bomb. President Obama &amp; Secretary of State Clinton got pretty much everyone in the world that mattered (including the EU, Russia, China, India, Japan, etc.) to impose crippling sanctions on Iran, which eventually brought them to the table. Not only will we have gone eight years with no Iranian nuclear weapons, but President Obama will leave office with Iran’s nuclear program out of commission for many years into the future.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;verdana&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif; font-size: x-small;">(<b>Brin aside:&nbsp;</b>Twenty five tons of enriched Uranium eliminated and Iran’s plutonium reactor filled with cement. Attacking Iran wouldn’t have come close to achieving that.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Moreover even a little rapprochement with Iran let’s us do what Nixon did, by going to China… play Iran and Saudi Arabia off each other, instead of being played.)</span><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">President Obama did what Bush only promised but failed to do in seven years: <b>He got Bin Laden.</b> Please repeat that sentence as many times as it takes to sink in. And we have had no major act of foreign terrorism on U.S. soil during his presidency.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">He finally ended our pointless 55 year Cold War diplomatic freeze with Cuba. And the Florida Cuban-expat community is gearing up to start businesses that will undermine communism the smart way.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">He added over two million acres of Wilderness Area and over 1000 river miles to the protections of the Wild and Scenic Rivers Act.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">He reformed the student loan program, cutting out redundant middle men and using the billions of dollars in savings to increase Pell grants. Granted, it will take a new Congress to end the nasty provision that declares student loans to be the only kind that cannot be refinanced.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">Oh, and despite&nbsp;24/7&nbsp;right wing media hyperventilation for weeks, not a single American died of Ebola contracted in the U.S.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">The national abortion rate declined roughly 15% under President Obama. And it wasn't because of increased restrictions in some states - in those states, abortions actually went up (they are the same states that make family planning, women's health services and contraception more difficult to access). If it was just due to restrictions, then you would expect teenage pregnancies and births to increase. Instead, they went down, as well.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">And there is much, much more.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;">If he was a Republican they would be naming airports after him. An aircraft carrier.&nbsp;But listening to Republicans, you’d think he has been a disaster. It is the centerpiece of every GOP candidate’s campaign rant that President Obama has been a disaster!&nbsp; Only note the lack of actual statistics. Outcomes. Comparison of results.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">== A Brin remise ==</b><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Me again, in awe of how well Russ makes this crucial point, how <i>for your own pragmatic self interest,</i> you should never again allow this generation/type of republicans anywhere near a burnt match, let alone a modern, entrepreneurial economy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">(There used to be grownup republicans who liked science and facts – I even know some of these relics!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>May they be seeds for a restored, mature conservatism, out of the coming ashes.)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I will only add this.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>If you look at the zillionaires who are democrats… or else libertarians who avoid the GOP like the plague … you’ll see that these are the tech guys who have actually invested in new products, services, and productive capacity.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">How ironic! The ones who are enhancing our economy on the supply side are the ones who despise the tax-tomfoolery-voodoo called “<a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2010/02/a-primer-on-supply-side-vs-demand-side.html">Supply Side Economics</a>” – a GOP religious dogma that never had <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">one</i> successful prediction or positive outcome to its credit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Ever.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">It is the other type of mogul – those rich from resource extraction subsidized off public lands, or from inheritance or rent-seeking or Wall Street manipulation, who invested almost none of their Supply Side tax cut largesse in new, productive enterprise, who spend lavishly instead on cheating, bribing officials and buying elections, with the core aim of keeping Supply Side voodoo alive.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Go figure. Only know this.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Ever more of the smart ones are seeing what’s in their own self interest.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>As Joe Kennedy said – (I paraphrase) - when his fellow moguls yelled at him, for supporting FDR:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">“If Roosevelt’s reforms make the working class happy and healthy and prosperous, I’ll get to keep half my wealth.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>That’s better than clutching it tight, then losing it all in revolution.”<o:p></o:p></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">===</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh, I promised to offer my comments on the New Hampshire primary... but this posting is too long. &nbsp;So I will give them below, as the first comment in this thread. &nbsp;Chime in with your own! &nbsp;We have a great, lively blog-cummunity (blogmunity?) down there! &nbsp;Maybe a bit intellectual... ah well.</span></div><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml> <o:OfficeDocumentSettings> <o:AllowPNG/> </o:OfficeDocumentSettings></xml><![endif]--> <!--[if gte mso 9]><xml> <w:WordDocument>
