storm of politics<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2015/11/amateurs-in-the-oval-office/407830/" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="color: black; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Okay, skim down for links to weightier postings by some big thinkers about U.S. politics. &nbsp;But if you have the patience for some ... er... <i>unusual</i>&nbsp;insights, start here.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">First -- <a href="http://www.newyorker.com/humor/borowitz-report/cruz-victory-gives-hope-to-despised-people-everywhere">this piece of lovely satire by Andy Borowitz </a>about how, completely aside from any policy or cultural issue, the victory of Ted Cruz in Iowa has given heart to America's most despised minority -- Nasty Folks who are hated by their peers: &nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">"</span>In the wake of the Iowa caucuses, America’s most unlikeable people were lighting up Facebook with comments in praise of Cruz, bursting with pride that one of their own - the despicably unpleasant and deservedly friendless - had a legitimate shot at the White House." </i>&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Ha.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>Turning more serious, here's a political weird-thought of the week: </b>There has been a perfect storm striking the re-ignited Confederacy -- formerly called the Republican Party. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>1- The oil price plunge</i> has hurt the secret masters of the GOP, sapping their eagerness to spend.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>2- Meanwhile the PAC putsch</i> -- attempting to buy American democracy -- has run into a wall. Vast sums did nothing to reverse the plummet of Jeb Bush, nor has cash had much visible effect on other races.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Sure, big retail states like Florida may bring money back to the fore.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>Still, what's an oligarch to do? What has come of America when elections are getting harder to buy?<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>3- Prediction.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>We will very soon discover that much of that secret-master PAC money has shifted to social media.</i><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; For example, m</span>any of the angriest-sounding, most vehemently anti-Clinton folks on the Sanders sites - especially anon or pseudonymous folks - will be found to be <i>agents provocateurs - </i>(look up the term) -&nbsp;under pay to drive wedges through the Democratic coalition.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">What?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>You think there’s any way on Earth that’s <i>not</i>true, at least in some large fraction of cases? What would <i>you</i>&nbsp;do, if you were David Koch?<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">It won’t work. </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Sanders himself will staunch that, knowing that <i>“it’s the Supreme Court, stupid.”</i>&nbsp;He's already made clear that he and Secretary Clinton will each come down hard on any of their supporters who don't, later, converge behind the nominee.</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Still, my advice to emotional Sandersites is this: Fight for Bernie! But don't be like the irrationally sanctimonious Baby Boomers. Be logical and positive, then kiss and make up, whoever wins the nom.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">And if your blood is still up, then turn youthful vigor to your<i> local state assembly race,</i> where one more volunteer could wreak a seismically important shift! And where the candidate will know you by na</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">me.<o:p></o:p></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">4- Okay, okay, there are some old fart boomers doing the same damn thing.<span style="background-color: white;">&nbsp;Madeleine Albright made <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2016/02/08/us/politics/gloria-steinem-madeleine-albright-hillary-clinton-bernie-sanders.html?_r=0">the amazing statement</a> that "there's a special kind of hell" for women who don't support Clinton, and Gloria Steinem managed to top that, telling the press that young women supporting Sanders where "just doing it to please the boys." Argh, such arrogance. Well, well. These are fools, part of a foolishly emotional generation. But certainly not on the payroll of any Koch PAC.&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: white;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: white;">Geez get it through your heads, boomers. This is no longer about you.</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">5-<i> Wild card Donald Trump </i>has been especially hard on the republica</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">n establishment, hammering Roger Ailes's Fox News -- the Murdoch-Saudi, Confederacy-rousing, poison machine. Their formula worked for years, stirring populist fury among lower middle class whites, using immigrants, scientists, teachers and all other "smartypants elites" as objects of ire, in order to distract from growing wealth disparity.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">But working class whites can only be diverted this way for so long, without <i>one of two</i> things happening:<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span>-- The first possible outcome – that we saw tragically happen in Germany, 80 years ago, will be if this fervid, right wing populism stampedes even farther into crazy land, yanking the reins out of Roger Ailes's hands, much the way Junkers lords found the horse they had spurred into a froth running away with them, toward a cliff. You reap what you sow.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Or else --<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">-- <i>or else</i> many in the tea party activist wing might (just might) start to remember their parents in the Greatest Generation. Heroes who overcame the Depression and Hitler and Stalin and built those halcyon days of the 1950s and 1960s that non-college white Americans so yearn for -- days of mighty capitalist entrepreneurship that happened under high, Rooseveltean tax rates. And those working class whites may start to wonder: <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>"Say… did my folks know something, about class struggle, that I don't know? Like suspicion of oligarchy? And why should I keep drinking koolaid offered by oligarchs?"&nbsp;</i></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">What happens to the Murdoch-Saudi game plan when white boomers ponder that Greatest Generation, and remember that their parents' favorite living human was Franklin Delano Roosevelt?</span><br /><i style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"><br /></i><br /><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sSStgaHsSW4/VrfTxoSe70I/AAAAAAAAOa4/Tn9hC710zxs/s1600/trump-sanders-2016.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="210" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sSStgaHsSW4/VrfTxoSe70I/AAAAAAAAOa4/Tn9hC710zxs/s320/trump-sanders-2016.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">6</span><i style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">- Hence my final weird fantasy.</i><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"> Only a science fiction author would or could concoct this one.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp; And to be clear I do not favor this weird thing!</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">And yet there is a scenario for some populists out there to start pushing it. A nascent, super-populist movement for </span><b style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">TRUMP-SANDERS... or else SANDERS-TRUMP.</b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Sound insane? &nbsp;Of course it is! But Robert Heinlein predicted America would pass through "The Crazy Years." &nbsp;Anyway, the more you ponder the wild idea, the more likely it seems that someone – somewhere on our populist-frothing internet - will raise a banner.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== Are there "cycles" to politics? ==</span></b><br /><b><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></b></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2015/11/amateurs-in-the-oval-office/407830/">Jonathan Rauch notes the rule of 14</a>&nbsp;--&nbsp;<i>"No one gets elected president who needs longer than 14 years to get from his or her first gubernatorial or Senate victory to either the presidency or the vice presidency"&nbsp;</i>-- may be coming to an end. Hillary Clinton was elected to the Senate 16 years ago. Jeb Bush to his governorship18 years ago.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">On the other hand, many of this year's leading candidates have little or no political or military experience. A reflection of an underlying public preference for presidents who are battle-tested but not battle-weary, experienced enough to know their way around but fresh enough to bring new energy to the job.&nbsp;</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></span><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-eiXziPEpaqw/VplrVT91pYI/AAAAAAAAOP0/NBK-OofAXYU/s1600/presidential-experience-election-year.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-eiXziPEpaqw/VplrVT91pYI/AAAAAAAAOP0/NBK-OofAXYU/s320/presidential-experience-election-year.jpg" width="320" /></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">See a chart from The Atlantic that shows<a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2015/11/amateurs-in-the-oval-office/407830/">&nbsp;the experience level of presidential winners and losers from 1960 to 2012</a>. Starting in 1996, the candidate with more experience begins consistently losing. Moreover, as the trend lines show, the inexperience premium has increased over time.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Two generations ago, James Q. Wilson wrote in&nbsp;<a href="http://www.amazon.com/Amateur-Democrat-Politics-Three-Cities/dp/0226900991/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20"><i>The Amateur Democrat</i></a>&nbsp;that political amateurs who were unyielding in their righteousness had begun supplanting political professionals who were willing to make deals and compromise. The ascendency of amateurism, he predicted, would cause social friction and governmental gridlock: 'Political conflict will be intensified, social cleavages will be exaggerated, party leaders will tend to be men skilled in the rhetorical arts, and the party's ability to produce agreement by trading issue-free resources will be reduced.'<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Time to shrug off the boomers’ self-indulgent trips and snap out of this.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/02/a-perfect-storm-of-politics.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)44tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-5316620634920104872Sat, 06 Feb 2016 21:14:00 +00002016-02-06T14:15:21.392-08:00bcibig questionsfuturequestionsquoratechnological changesBig questions for the future<div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The Big Questions Contests aim to expand Quora’s already marvelous system for posing quandaries and getting fascinating answers.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">For example “How can we&nbsp;<a href="https://www.quora.com/What-constraints-to-AI-and-machine-learning-algorithms-are-needed-to-prevent-AI-from-becoming-a-dystopian-threat-to-humanity"><i>prevent runaway AI (</i><span style="color: windowtext; text-decoration: none; text-underline: none;">Artificial Intelligence)</span><i>from becoming a dystopian threat to humanity?</i></a>”&nbsp; Interesting discussions!&nbsp; <a href="https://www.quora.com/What-constraints-to-AI-and-machine-learning-algorithms-are-needed-to-prevent-AI-from-becoming-a-dystopian-threat-to-humanity/answer/David-Brin">My own suggestion </a>– unlike any other – was re-published on Forbes, in an article titled:&nbsp;<a href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/quora/2016/01/29/the-one-thing-we-need-to-stop-robots-from-achieving-world-domination/#2064cad96dcf">The one thing we need to stop robots from achieving world domination</a>.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://www.quora.com/What-technological-changes-will-create-the-most-opportunities-for-new-startups-over-the-next-2-3-years" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="color: black;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-3wPcgsLCAx4/Vq1diOdZN2I/AAAAAAAAOWs/k0etfmPPouA/s320/technological-changes.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Another Quora contest question asks: “</span><span style="color: #262626; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="https://www.quora.com/What-technological-changes-will-create-the-most-opportunities-for-new-startups-over-the-next-2-3-years">What technological changes will create the most opportunities for new startups over the next 2-3 years?</a></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">” My answer?</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I believe the nearest and most blatantly obvious, transformational shift will come from the micro-biome. Within two to five years there will be an end to voodoo-guesswork-yoghurt-based "probiotics." They will be replaced by far more specific and well-understood implantations we can add to our digestive tracts (from both directions), as well as skin and other crevices, with major effects on individual and mass health.</span></div><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Why so quickly? Because although there is a dizzying array of these firmicutes and other bacterial genuses in our guts and skin etc... the variety is actually fairly limited and very, very linear. Various versions of Moore's Law (in computation, sensing, genetic analysis) will cross the microbiome's complexity in very rapid order. Big studies - some already underway - will nail down how these bug-zoos correlate with your genes, body type, heredity, diet...<o:p></o:p>...and truly useful prescriptions and lifestyle and diet recommendations will issue forth quite rapidly, enabling us to both add beneficial microbiota and target species that currently wreak harm. For example by forcing upon us low-level, erosive&nbsp;inflammations.<o:p></o:p></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">There are many other biomedical miracles on the horizon, of course. But most of those -- in the genome, proteome, regulatome, connectome and so on -- get exponentially more complex as we dive in. Hence, our tools must improve at an ever-increasing rate, just to keep stepping forward. The same appears not to be true of the microbiome, whose linearity and limited needed dataset make me certain it will se amazing developments in just 3-5 years. <o:p></o:p></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== More opportunities on the tech horizon ==</b></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="http://www.amazon.com/The-Industries-Future-Alec-Ross/dp/1476753652/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><span style="color: black;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Vhpw3OP_t7c/Vq1qCOPgl3I/AAAAAAAAOW8/7WYxHVNYXBU/s320/41uraIPjHCL._SX332_BO1%252C204%252C203%252C200_.jpg" width="214" /></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/peterdecherney/2016/01/30/a-bad-time-to-be-a-control-freak-alec-ross-forecasts-the-industries-of-the-future/#2715e4857a0b286305cf209c">Where should we look for the next Silicon Valley</a>?&nbsp;What industries will survive -- and which are likely to perish in the near future? In his new book, <a href="http://www.amazon.com/The-Industries-Future-Alec-Ross/dp/1476753652/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">Industries of the Future</a>, Alex Ross peers ahead to the next decade to identify major global trends and technological forces driving innovation and pervasive social change. Openness and transparency will be critical requirements for success in both business and government. Ross notes, "the 21st century is a terrible time to be a control freak," for the next stage for innovation is more likely to arise in "50 different versions of Silicon Valley, all unique from each other and all focusing on different domains."</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i><br /></i></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>How soon will we see workable brain - computer interfaces? &nbsp;</i></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The first dry-electrode, portable and commercially off the shelf 64-channel&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.kurzweilai.net/ucsd-spinoffs-create-lab-quality-portable-64-channel-eeg-headset?utm_source=KurzweilAI+Weekly+Newsletter&amp;utm_campaign=bf9d4e2d1b-UA-946742-1&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_term=0_147a5a48c1-bf9d4e2d1b-281972889" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">wearable brain-computer interface&nbsp;</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">(BCI) has been developed by bioengineers and cognitive scientists associated with UCSD Jacobs School. <a href="https://www.technologyreview.com/s/600686/government-seeks-high-fidelity-brain-computer-interface/">Obama's Brain Mapping Project </a>seeks to better understand and map the neural activity of the brain. Meanwhile,&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">Harvard is trying to build an&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.wired.co.uk/news/archive/2016-01/25/harvard-brain-ai-neuroscience" style="font-family: '&quot;arial&quot;', '&quot;helvetica&quot;', sans-serif;">AI as fast as the human brain</a><span style="font-family: &quot;\22 arial\22 &quot; , &quot;\22 helvetica\22 &quot; , sans-serif;">.</span><br /><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Is evolution in the natural world at all “tendentious” (directional)… or even propulsive… in directions that might be called “intelligent?&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style="color: #191919;">A computer scientist and a biologist&nbsp;<a href="http://www.kurzweilai.net/why-evolution-may-be-intelligent-based-on-deep-learning?utm_source=KurzweilAI+Weekly+Newsletter&amp;utm_campaign=bf9d4e2d1b-UA-946742-1&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_term=0_147a5a48c1-bf9d4e2d1b-281972889">propose to unify the theory of evolution with learning theories</a>&nbsp;to explain the “amazing, apparently intelligent designs that evolution produces.”&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Meanwhile, human design work looks more like nature. Drone evolution moves quickly, with now an ecological niche for&nbsp;<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">predatory “falcons”</i>&nbsp;--&nbsp;<a href="http://www.kurzweilai.net/robotic-falcon-can-capture-retrieve-renegade-drones?utm_source=KurzweilAI+Weekly+Newsletter&amp;utm_campaign=bf9d4e2d1b-UA-946742-1&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_term=0_147a5a48c1-bf9d4e2d1b-281972889">a drone catcher that can pursue and capture rogue drones</a>&nbsp;that might threaten military installations, air traffic, sporting events, and even the White House.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>Wow, watch it spit a net over the intruder and draw it in.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>I want one!</span><br /><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">How do parts of the brain communicate? With around 200 billion neurons in a single human brain, and the possibility of hundreds of thousands of synapse connections from a single neuron, the brain can process a vast amount of information. Yet, a hundred trillion active synapses aren’t all there is.</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">We now know that there is chemical information exchange between neurons and neighboring glial or astrocyte cells.</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Also there is increasing evidence suggesting that intracellular computing may take place, perhaps as many as a hundred thousand transactions per synapse flash.</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Is that plenty?</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Well, now research suggests that&nbsp;<a href="http://futurism.com/links/brain-may-send-message-using-electric-field/">we may use&nbsp;</a></span><i style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"><a href="http://futurism.com/links/brain-may-send-message-using-electric-field/">electrical fields</a></i><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://futurism.com/links/brain-may-send-message-using-electric-field/">&nbsp;to communicate information</a>&nbsp;across different sections of the brain.</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Well, well, some of us expected this.</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Take the “standing wave” of consciousness that I speculate about, in both&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/earth.html">EARTH</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/kilnpeople.html">KILN PEOPLE</a>.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #475658; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b style="color: black; font-family: -webkit-standard;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">== And more science still! ==</span></b></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Quantum-Handshake-Entanglement-Nonlocality-Transactions/dp/3319246402/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="color: black;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5z9w9OaA_Ks/Vq1a6EiPMSI/AAAAAAAAOWg/n3x9EpgLHR0/s320/quantum-handshake-cramer.jpg" width="212" /></span></a></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">How has quantum mechanics expanded our understanding of time and the cosmos? My friend and colleague John Cramer’s new book on the translational interpretation of quantum mechanics, entitled <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Quantum-Handshake-Entanglement-Nonlocality-Transactions/dp/3319246402/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">The Quantum Handshake- Entanglement, Nonlocality and Transactions</a>&nbsp;has just been&nbsp;published by Springer (ISBN: 978-3-319-24640-6). It is available at the Springer <a href="http://www.springer.com/gp/book/9783319246406">website</a>&nbsp;or on <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Quantum-Handshake-Entanglement-Nonlocality-Transactions/dp/3319246402/?_encoding=UTF8&amp;tag=contbrin-20">Amazon</a>.</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Researchers have developed a remarkable new&nbsp;</span><a href="http://futurism.com/links/french-scientists-invents-breakthrough-bone-cement-foam-to-repair-and-heal-bone-problems/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">injectable bone foam</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;that not only repairs bone damage but also allows bone formation.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Kyocera's fourth&nbsp;<a href="http://www.popularmechanics.com/science/green-tech/a19071/worlds-largest-floating-solar-power-plant-kyocera-solar/">floating solar power plant in Japan</a>&nbsp;will suspend modules on the surface of a reservoir. It’s the latest in a series of innovative solar plants, such as India's&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.popularmechanics.com/technology/infrastructure/news/a16986/cochin-airport-solar-power/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">solar powered airport</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;and ambitious plan to&nbsp;</span><a href="http://www.popularmechanics.com/science/green-tech/news/a16516/indias-ingenious-solar-canals/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">cover canals with sun-harvesting panels</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Prehistoric massacres... Wow, archaeological proof of how far back go our ways of war. <span style="color: #262626;">Of 12 relatively complete skeletons recently unearthed at the shores of Lake Turkana, in Kenya, 10 showed unmistakable signs of violent death, <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2016/01/21/science/prehistoric-massacre-ancient-humans-lake-turkana-kenya.html?_r=0">the scientists said.</a> Partial remains of at least 15 other persons were found at the site and are thought to have died in the same attack.</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.upi.com/Science_News/2016/01/22/Scientists-weave-together-nanomaterials-for-the-first-time/6461453482922/">Woven nano-materials</a> may have a wide variety of uses that require exceptional resiliency,&nbsp;strength and flexibility.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The Defense Threat Reduction Agency has awarded a $1 million grant to UCSD to develop <a href="http://jacobsschoolofengineering.blogspot.com/2016/01/nanoengineers-win-1-million-grant-to.html">new skin-wearable systems</a> that can rapidly and efficiently detect chemical and biological agents.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span>The proposed wearable epidermal sensors will also be equipped with therapeutic agents that are released upon detection of the chemical and biological threats.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">See the extent of&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/energy-environment/wp/2016/01/18/this-is-where-90-percent-of-global-warming-is-going/" style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">warming of the oceans.</a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;The actual, non-fox’d science.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">But of course the real alarm bell is ocean&nbsp;</span><i style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">acidification</i><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">It is utterly demonstrable, clearly happening and no one has even proposed a reason, other than human generated CO2.</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Denialist cultists hurry to change the subject, whenever the words “ocean acidification” come up. Try it and watch what happens! Sane people need to start using those words more often!&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Heck it’s getting so blatant that even Forbes is allowing articles like this one, showing that&nbsp;<i>science and denialism are opposites,</i>&nbsp;at least&nbsp;<a href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/ericmack/2016/01/18/todays-oceans-are-different-than-they-were-twenty-years-ago/#2715e4857a0b2cd39ecd14fb">when it comes to the oceans.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;When this happens on Forbes, you know that some folks in the oligarchy have started realizing, they need the planet, too.&nbsp;</span></div><div class="MsoNormal"><br /></div><div class="blogger-post-footer">. . ...a collaborative contrarian product of David Brin, Enlightenment Civilization, obstinate human nature... and http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/ (site feed URL: http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/atom.xml)</div>http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2016/02/big-questions-for-future.htmlnoreply@blogger.com (David Brin)48tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8587336.post-6051763455045934657Wed, 03 Feb 2016 17:01:00 +00002016-02-03T09:02:38.811-08:00bernie sanderselection 2016iowa returnsobama state of the unionpaul krugmanpragmatic politicsspeechtrumpismIowa, Inanity, SOTU and political games<div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">In the wake of those frenzied and overblown Iowa Caucuses, a number of interesting thoughts:</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">1) That Donald Trump should have done a little traditional Expectations Dampening - you know, like politicians do. But that is not in his nature. &nbsp;Anyone could tell you (as I did) that Iowan conservatives are very religious and that faction turns out - hence Cruz was always the leader there, whatever the polls say. (Weirdly, Iowa democrats turn out to be way more <i>leftist</i>&nbsp;than liberals nationwide. &nbsp;What a state.) In any event: <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/the-fix/wp/2016/02/02/the-bad-news-for-ted-cruz-his-iowa-win-looks-very-similar-to-mike-huckabees-and-rick-santorums/?%3Ftid%3D=sm_pg">"The bad news for Ted Cruz: His Iowa win looks very similar to Mike Huckabee’s and Rick Santorum’s."</a></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Only I still maintain Cruz has a cunning plan.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">2) The near tie between Clinton and Sanders is actually great news for democrats. Both candidates will benefit from lively and invigorating tension. But this assumes Bernie is able to keep perspective and not get so caught up that he forgets -- you are vying, vigorously, for captaincy of a team you both know must win. Bruise each other... a little... but not too much for genuine hugs and kisses, later.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Oh and Hill? No thumbs on the scale. A cute trick would be to offer Bernie at-minimum the right to pick your Inspector General and your SEC head. No quid pro quo. &nbsp;Just offer it.</span><br /><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-U-57O9ATezA/VrFJ35FRSeI/AAAAAAAAOXM/xSsVFi-IZUE/s1600/krugman.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-U-57O9ATezA/VrFJ35FRSeI/AAAAAAAAOXM/xSsVFi-IZUE/s320/krugman.jpg" width="316" /></a><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">3)&nbsp;NYT Nobelist economist Paul Krugman </span><a href="http://krugman.blogs.nytimes.com/2016/02/02/post-iowa-notes/" style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">highlights ‘uplift’</a><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"> in his analysis of the Iowa returns.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Yes, he chose that word. His point being that we should choose to be more ambitious -- the one core thought that Bernie Sanders has contributed. <b>Can we ‘uplift’ our society, our civilization?&nbsp;</b></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Right now, the American public mood is addicted to downer memes, despite almost every statistical metric having improved. While science fiction <i>is</i> filled with many negative stories, <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/idiotplot.html">often unecessarily so</a>, it remains the one medium where perhaps 10% of the time, we see <i>real optimism and hope</i>. Prof. Krugman knows this, else why would he feature a Michael Whelan sci fi cover to <a href="http://krugman.blogs.nytimes.com/2016/02/02/post-iowa-notes/">illustrate his essay?</a></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span class="yiv7824068526" style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span class="yiv7824068526" style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;">4) Did I mention demmie 'hugs?' Among many young Sanders supporters I have been noting a bit of a <i>shrill tone,</i> even hatred for the Clintonite Democratic 'establishment.' And sure, some degree of complaint about that is valid. And yet, I am from the 1960s, and you kids are pure amateurs at indignation. Seriously? Some persepective is called-for. Especially when some bright-bozos have been proclaiming that "radicalism" is preferable to "well-meaning but too-moderate incrementalism."</span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span class="yiv7824068526" style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span class="yiv7824068526" style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;">The implication is that pragmatic moderate are tepid in desiring reform. But i</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;">ndeed, I warned about the threat of a secret world oligarchy in my novel <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/earth.html">Earth</a> way back in 1989 -- see my portrayal of the "Helvetian war" -- and no one dissects that trend more often or deeply than I do. Also, that novel was early re Climate Change warnings.</span><br /><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;">Do I agree with much that Sanders says? Sure. I am glad of some of the radical enthusiasm he's fired up. And note that PAC money is playing a much smaller role in this election. Cool.</span><br /><span style="font-family: arial, helvetica, sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-IrCPKV4zZpk/VrFK1U4jbgI/AAAAAAAAOXU/HiADqweay0k/s1600/pragmatists.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="236" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-IrCPKV4zZpk/VrFK1U4jbgI/AAAAAAAAOXU/HiADqweay0k/s320/pragmatists.jpg" width="320" /></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Still,<i> the world is ultimately made by pragmatists and incrementalists.</i> Franklin Roosevelt reset capitalism and gave the workers such a big stake that it created the fantastic American</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">middle class</span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">. Which oligarchs are busy undermining, sure. So? All that means is another Rooseveltean reset is needed. &nbsp;Hey, if our parents in the Greatest Generation could achieve that miracle, without diluting the best aspects of creative-competitive capitalism at all -- then we should be able to, as well.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Only dig this well, The New Deal had some radical aspects! But deep down, a</span><span style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;">nyone who knew Franklin Roosevelt also knew that he was above all a politician, a pragmatist, an arm twister, and a moderate. A negotiator! The only way you can reconcile those two facts is by recognizing this: <i>radicals will not accomplish as much in the American context as fierce pragmatists will.&nbsp;</i></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;helvetica&quot; , &quot;arial&quot; , sans-serif; white-space: pre-wrap;">And we must do our part. Obama or Clinton needed us to give them a Congress. Any failure of their incrementalism was our fault. And "radicals" without a Congress will be even more pathetically ineffective.</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Congress listens -- in sullen crankiness ==</b></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">President Obama’s <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2016/01/12/politics/state-of-the-union-2016-transcript-full-text/">State of the Union address</a> (SOTU) got a lot of attention, including nervy Paul Ryan, who either smirked "knowingly" or else scowled, theatrically-disrespectful through the entire address, <a href="http://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/elections/2016/01/13/paul-ryan-obama-political-state-of-the-union-degrades-presidency/78747316/">then accused Obama of </a>“degrading” the office of president… this from the party that gave us Richard Nixon and both Saudi-Bushes.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MPjGZKgdF5I/VpkmFq7XBxI/AAAAAAAAOO8/Xq5cnmTswMU/s1600/1156953_1280x720.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="color: black;"><img border="0" height="207" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-MPjGZKgdF5I/VpkmFq7XBxI/AAAAAAAAOO8/Xq5cnmTswMU/s320/1156953_1280x720.jpg" width="320" /></span></a><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Obama’s content – appealing for a return to the politics of actual-negotiation – was in fact filled with things to which we might all reasonably agree.&nbsp; But one topic I have long inveighed against… electoral cheating. Especially gerrymandering&nbsp; -- &nbsp;<i>"the practice of drawing our congressional districts so that politicians can pick their voters, and not the other way around."</i><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><br /></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">This article appraises how easy it would be to <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2016/01/13/this-is-actually-what-america-would-look-like-without-gerrymandering/">create fair electoral maps based upon “compactness of districts</a>". In fact though, I do not agree with this solution – though it would be a vast improvement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">&nbsp; </span><a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/gerrymandering1.html">Elsewhere</a> I offer a ‘minimum overlap” proposal that would require just three sentences and end the problem in a shot. &nbsp;</span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><br /></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Only here I want to comment less on President Obama’s SOTU address than on South Carolina Governor <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2016-01-13/republican-haley-takes-aim-at-trump-in-party-s-response-to-obama">Nikki Haley's official GOP response</a>. The sub-text implications are quite interesting. <span style="color: #2e2e2e;">Haley admitted in an interview on CNN that her speech partly targeted Trump &amp; Cruz and that party leaders reviewed her speech before she delivered it Tuesday.</span> <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><br /></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Choosing her as SOTU responder was one of the few actions that the Republican establishment could take, having completely lost control over the wild presidential nomination race. Earlier, I suggested 1:3 odds that they are <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2015/12/wait-for-ryan-express.html">setting up Paul Ryan to step in</a>, should the convention be deadlocked after a first or second ballot (see below). (Ryan's scowl, all through the SOTU? A hour of silent-and-free publicity.) But back to Haley...<br style="mso-special-character: line-break;" /><!--[if !supportLineBreakNewLine]--><br style="mso-special-character: line-break;" /><!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">The GOP establishment knows that Jeb is toast and Rubio - their new boy - is unlikely.&nbsp; The Ryan Gambit is plausible, but their backup plan...?&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Set up their choice to be the VP running mate.</span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /><b>Let's back up a bit.</b> I believe Ted Cruz <i>never intended</i> to win the GOP presidential nod.&nbsp; He knows how hated he is, by the GOP lords. &nbsp;(In fact by almost anyone with normal intelligence.) His role model has to be Richard Nixon in 1952. And sure, if Jeb or Rubio or Ryan get the nom, then Cruz would be their shoe-in VP pick -- their envoy to the fundies and tea partiers, to keep them in line.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">What's Cruz's payoff?&nbsp; Either 4 or 8 years as VP, pulling in IOUs... or else, if the GOP ticket loses this year, becoming the heir apparent to oppose the sitting dem's re-election in 2020.<br /><br />Only now that plan is dashed!&nbsp; The rebels - Trump and Cruz - have been too successful! If Trump wins the nomination, he simply can't choose Cruz as his running mate. They'd torch the whole party. Donald would have to find a "moderate" to mollify the Lords and to soothe offended folks in Trump's wild wake. (Unless Trump then intends to dash-for-the-center! In which case Cruz might make sense as veep, after all.)<br /><br />Moreover, Ted Cruz - if by some chance he wins the main nom - would have to do the same.<br /><br />And so we arrive in South Carolina, where the most important Republican primary will be held. Nikki Haley will be potent there. Moreover, she is a solid VP choice for many reasons.&nbsp; A woman and a soother... and somewhat of an ethnic minority... though not Hispanic and not from a state the GOP needs. No matter! How better to reach out to GOP grownups and urge them to stay loyal, while either Cruz or Trump rampage about?</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Haley: <i>“It takes everyone to get their egos out of the room and really sit down and say, ‘OK, how are we going to get to a solution? That’s not something we’re seeing in D.C. right now.”</i></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Further: Haley said that Republicans share the blame with Democrats for the nation’s distrust of Washington and need to <i>“recognize our contributions to the erosion of the public trust in America’s leadership.”</i></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Look, it's possible she's even sincere about wanting to forge a path for American conservatism out of the hellish pit Roger Ailes led them. If so, then her getting a VP stint on a losing zombie-festival could be good news for us all, putting her in position to bring back some version of the party of Eisenhower, in 2020. &nbsp;It's a scenario.</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">I'll put no money on it though. &nbsp;I do know this... actually winning the Republican Party's presidential nomination in 2016 was <i>not</i>&nbsp;Ted Cruz's plan. As in <i>The Manchurian Candidate,</i>&nbsp;his scheme was a patient one, and now his prize, the VP slot, is slipping away from his hands, because he's been too successful. &nbsp;And I can just imagine him murmuring "Oh crap, now what!"</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><i>Summary:</i> If Trump or Cruz win the nom - VP goes to Haley or some hispanic GOP pol.</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">If it's anyone other than those two, then Cruz gets what he really wanted - (though perhaps sugar plum fairies are now dancing in his head) - the VP slot.</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><b>== Has Trumpism run its course? ==</b></span></div><div style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin: 0in;"><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Donal's lack of savvy expectations limiting before Iowa means his aura has taken a hit. So, is it over? Of course not. &nbsp;Still...</span><br /><span style="color: #2e2e2e; font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2016/01/the-eight-causes-of-trumpism/422427/" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><span style="color: black;"><img border="0" height="318" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-dRajnt4mD9g/Vplaqo_EubI/AAAAAAAAOPM/jnqSXTDhjIw/s320/trumpism.jpg" width="320" /></span></a></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2016/01/the-eight-causes-of-trumpism/422427/">The Eight Causes of Trumpism:</a>&nbsp;This stunningly cogent article from The Atlantic fills in the historical trends that - since 1990 - have contributed to turning American politics from being about policy argument and negotiation, to an utterly polarized hate-fest. <b>"The 8 causes of Trumpism" is actually not about Donald Trump, at all,</b> but the forces that made 1/3 of Americans so volcanically (and illogically) furious that only a manipulative outsider-savanarola like Trump or Cruz can be viewed as appealing.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><br /></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">There are factors that Mr. Ornstein leaves out.&nbsp; Like the role that Saudi investment played in building Fox News into the incendiary fuel behind a New Confederacy.&nbsp; Or how&nbsp; those petro-sheiks and our own coal barons created a populist frenzy that (to their chagrin) is now slipping out of their control, much the way Junker-class lords in 1920s Germany thought they could foster another right-wing populism, then lived to regret it.&nbsp;</span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Still, Ornstein does feature a crucial moment -- the treasonous know-nothing act when Newt Gingrich's House GOP dissolved its own Office of Technology Assessment, and sent all the techies and boffins and nerds packing, openly declaring that science and facts that conflict with dogma have no place within the Capitol walls..</span></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><br /></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;">Now that <a href="http://davidbrin.blogspot.com/2014/09/phases-of-american-civil-war.html">phase 8 of the American civil war</a> is thoroughly blatant, is it time, at last, to call it what it is? (Start ordering your blue-kepi 1865 caps now, for next Halloween!) Only then might the Blue Union do what it was forced to do, during other phases of this recurring, national fever.&nbsp; Win.&nbsp; Overwhelmingly.&nbsp; Then, "with charity for all," resuming our ambitious role in remaking a better world.</span></div><div style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><br /></span></div><a href="http://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/extension/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.blogger.com%2Fblogger.g%3FblogID%3D8587336%23editor&amp;media=https%3A%2F%2F1.bp.blogspot.com%2F-sex8zNHhd4I%2FVpls1s_XRoI%2FAAAAAAAAOQA%2FYBCOvJ3xuCs%2Fs1600%2Fdark-money-mayer-koch-brothers.jpeg&amp;xm=h&amp;xv=sa1.37.01&amp;xuid=0gf8CigKxCzi&amp;description=" style="background-color: transparent; , &quot;helvetica&quot; , sans-serif;"><span style="color: #1d1d1d;">To be released in March,&nbsp;<a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/insistenceofvision.html"><b>Insistence of Vision</b></a> will open doorways into possible (and mind-blowing) tomorrows and alternate realities. Through tales like <i>“Chrysalis”</i> and <i>“Transition Generation”</i> and <i>“Stones of Significance”</i>you’ll explore the consequences, if we get want we ask for.&nbsp; You’ll meet alien invaders unlike any other, in <i>“Mars Opposition” </i>and in <i>“The Logs.”</i>&nbsp; There is also a novella offering new drama from the <a href="http://www.davidbrin.com/uplift.html">Uplift Universe!</a>&nbsp;</span></span></span><br /><span style="font-family: &quot;arial&quot; , &quot;helvetica&quot;
